And it should be that the children's cautery iron should have subtlety according to their size, and likewise for the larger people; after three days cure his thigh from the cautery of butter until the scorching dies out; then apply other ointments until he heals properly, and let him rest on his back for forty days so that the wound is well healed; and it should be that his wounds are not irritated for a long time, so that the intestines do not escape when he wants to get up in bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to stand up, he should have a well-made bandage and wear it for forty more days; and with good rest, he should work little and guard against over-consuming food and drink, and not raise his voice too high; and when he follows this instruction, he is completely healed. And I will speak of the treatment of surgery in my chapter afterwards.
de la routure dou ventre	Regarding the rupture of the stomach
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, if you observe that they are no longer growing, then apply fire according to the quantity of the rupture using a cautery, taking one-third of the cup's content; after this, follow the treatment as we have instructed. And none of the old texts advised that the affected area should be treated with three angles of heat in the shape like this:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first sign is to make an incision and draw a line across the width of the tear, and another below, and firmly hold your hand with all the fire cautery. But the initial cauterizations are lighter and more fluid.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old age in no limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes into any limb, whether from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts long, and medical cure does not help, then it is necessary for it to be cauterized with the cautery called "point", and perform cauterizations according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and strength and location of twists and pain. If there is healing in the first cautery, that's good; if this doesn't work, do another one on top of it, because these practices are such that they must move towards the part of the body that is closest to it, so you must make cauterizations until the patient feels better.
de meselerie	In mixture
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The mixture must be heated to a high degree by the cautery's aid, and similarly for the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. If you see it being cauterized, take care lest the disease is in its beginning stages, and if it's treated according to what we've said in the division, so that it doesn't spread or remain, and you fear that corruption might pervade the whole body, then do this: .v. applications of cautery on the head: .i. near the forehead at nine o'clock, and the other towards the forehead at the end of hair; and .ij. on the .ij. corners, and .i. behind at the neck; and let your hand remain so that the cautery reaches up to the bone, and until the scabs come out fully allowing for the evaporation of the excess fluids; and cauterize it on the mouth according to what was done before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is spread everywhere and it becomes obvious that it's spreading, you should cauterize using these cauterizing methods we've mentioned: one on the nose, and two cauterizations on the spine at the neck, and seven cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one large on the sternum and another underneath, and two each on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the heels, and one for each joint in hands and feet, and on the creases of the palms; and be careful not to burn any nerves under the heel, do not cauterize anywhere on the bone of the fingers, and one on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when I do more cautery, I give him more help, and he benefits from it; and know that the patients do not feel pain during cautery as the healthy would, because their bodies are already thoroughly corrupted. And you should have large and small cauterizers according to limbs and joints, like what you will find in instructions for iron tools. After treatment, wash with flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
de enfleure	To swell
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling appears in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and bandages, and it doesn't heal, then you should make cauterizations on the limb according to the size of the limb; and let the cauterization go slightly into the red part of the flesh; then treat with ointments until it heals. And do a cauterization at both hands and feet and back, at the exit point of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and in this way, the swelling is removed; and still, no one should interfere if they don't know about limbs or how nerves move within the body.
de albaras	From burns
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease known as "albaras" is matured, and medicine does not help at all, then use a cautery to treat it slightly for some time, according to the amount of blood in the wound, until the pus is removed and its color changes; then cleanse with flour mixed with lentils and rose oil, and leaves from the plantain plant, as well as chicken blood and quail urine, each using one part of these ingredients. Mix them all together, wrap it with a cloth, and leave it on the wound until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for the sore by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the sore begins to appear, and you want to stop its spread, then use a cautery that seems like one circle, searing around the entire circumference of the sore. And still, some argue it's better to apply cautery also in the center of the sore; but I do not find this advisable at all, fearing it might lead to an ulceration and putrefaction, which is something I have already avoided on numerous occasions; a more straightforward approach would be to cauterize around with the "circular" type of cautery, as we explained in our discussion about different types of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the swelling which cannot perish
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease which is called "adubelati", and it takes time to die, either due to the excesses that it causes or because of old age in the body when it becomes decrepit (meaning too old) and it has little blood, or because of tension; and you see it hasten towards death: then cauterize internally with several small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it like this. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that it is pierced all through the cautery, then heat up the cautery as described here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of that disease which is called 'adubelati' as long as the cauteries have pierced through the flesh, and use those cauteries such that the patient feels relief in such a way that the course of decay is alleviated. After cure until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment with fire using a hot iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another method of disease is called 'corrodens', and it's nothing else but a member lesion, for it consumes limbs just like the fire reduces dry wood. If you can apply a cautery with fire to this disease, then shape your hot irons in various sizes small and large, according to where on the body or where the illness is; after that cauterize from all sides until you remove every corruption, leaving nothing behind so that all that has been corrupted is removed. And let it be for three days, and while the burns from the fire heal, bear with suffering from the oil, removing all infections and corruption. After this treatment of ointments causing injury.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The text "des porrelz qui vienent as piez" translates to "the stones that come towards the bones" in English. This seems to describe a medical issue related to stones or deposits moving towards bone structures, which could be a description of gallstones, kidney stones, or other similar conditions in medieval medical terminology.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes it happens that within the foot develops a sickness which is called "gout" according to our understanding, and it's a large hard thing causing pain in the foot. And for this type of disease, there are two ways of using cautery. This means fire cautery, and hot water cautery. Fire cautery involves heating one tool like a feather from a chicken, making it similar to a needle, made of good iron sized so that it could pierce all around the nail, and having small margins; after doing this, heat up the entire tool on the nail until your hand gets red while holding the needle right at the end; then leave it there for three days until pus begins to form; afterwards, make a plaster with crushed garlic mixed with oil, apply the plaster overnight over the whole area, and the nails will fall out from their roots. Then treat the foot with an ointment that heals the flesh until it's healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are located within the body and occur in hands and feet, it's necessary that you use hot water cautery; and do so like this: take a spider hair or iron rod, or a feather from a chicken, place them on the nail and around it; this is for warts. Place the rod such that it burns all around it, then add some hot water, keep your hand firmly while applying pressure in a circular motion until the edge of the rod reaches to the root of the nail and manages to penetrate deeply into the hot water reaching up to the root; allow the patient to tolerate this for an hour with mild burning sensation. Then leave them like this, and they will all be pulled out from their roots. Repeat this process until you've treated all those in the body, then apply ointments that heal the flesh afterwards.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment involves shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When there are trembles due to cold or nerves, or fever of the fourteenth day or other similar conditions, it is necessary that you perform 4 or 5 cauteries on each of the spine points of the back. One cautery between each spinal point; and one on the chest under the olive cautery; if this continues, hasten the patient's recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	pus-filled sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Whenever pus-filled sores or pustules appear due to the bath of corruption, or from large rotten materials, it is necessary that they come from decayed substances. When they first show up, it's appropriate at once for each head of the pustule: a fine cautery made from the bark of myrtle, where the tip is heated by fire, or from the long root of aristolochia, or with the lentil-shaped cautery. And one should not cauterize them when they first appear according to this manner; instead, it discharges the excess that causes them and renders them healthy. But it's necessary for this to be done after blood has been evacuated.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great hemorrhages of the artery occur from where it is cut in the wound that reaches to the opposite side, or at incision of the abscess, or with the cautery on the limb, and similar situations; and it is a very grievous thing to occlude.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to any person, if you quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and hold it firmly until the pulse becomes quiet under your finger, and no more drops escape; then heat several olive oil cauteries of various sizes until they are all red. Then take one, or a larger or smaller according to the size of the wound and the location where the artery is located, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your index finger, and keep the cautery there until the pulse becomes still again.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are off the fire, then quickly take another one of the cauteries that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And never stop doing this one after the other until the bone is fully healed; and be careful not to burn the nerve that's nearby, and that no harm comes upon the patient; and know that when there is a break in an artery, it can't be mended very well by itself when the artery is large, unless done through one of the four ways we've mentioned: by cautery, or extraction if not already treated, or with strong stringing, or with medicines placed which have power to mend blood; and then tie and hold in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will provide for the mending by tightly binding with cloths or by putting heat sources on, or other similar things, if they do not benefit unless so prescribed.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no medicine or remedy at hand, should apply their finger on the wound site as we said before, and spread it well until the wound and the vein are mended upon it; and do not move his hand but keep it moist with cold water often till it becomes very cold until the bone is frozen, swollen, and mended. And perform cautery and medicine preparations for what needs them.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments for surgery
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have explained in the first chapter all diseases where it is necessary to use a fire cautery or hot medicine, and we discussed their causes, instruments, and forms. I put that chapter up until the foot, and I will proceed through this chapter using the same path as what seems easier for those who want it.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this one, you should know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first about the cauteries, so it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to embark on foolishness. For many ways of people come into treatments. Some come from those who are so afflicted by their illness that they die lightly because of the absurdity they find in their sickness, and the horror of their disease; and towards these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And concerning these I give you their meaning, and say: "wait, I am a physician"; illness is deceitful. It would not be proper for you to agree with those who come to your aid in this manner, but rather place more caution on your honor than on your greed, do not act foolishly but wisely of those whom you are certain of, and have taken care of; use prediction and indication in treatments for the health that is converted from your patients; and this will help you gain good reputation, glory, and long-lasting memory. And it will assist you to acquire a valuable renown.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lords give us good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have arranged this chapter in devising by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter on cauteries, which I have devised from head to feet, because you will find it more easily of that which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	at the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the mother constrains the head of the child too tightly; and sometimes it occurs due to a response reason that one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than children, and among all those I have observed, their death hastened; for which reason it seems to me that it would be better to divide the work of this chapter into these cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child of this, the shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day so much that it could no longer bear it; and believed to such moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled under the bone near the elbow, between the chest and the bone; and the muscles are like these when moisture is between the chest and the bone, and abscesses are small, that you cut in the middle of the head a wide crack; and let it be so long as two fists, as long as the moisture flows; and see this form of the syphilitic:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in a manner like an X, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see that the edges of the head are opened from each part, and the water spurts out when you press it from your hand inside, and this is not relieved: then you must make three cuts in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after making the incision, remove all moisture. After stopping the cuts from bleeding with bandages and powders, and applying wine and oil, let it be this way for up to five days; then reset the dislocation, treat the wound with different methods and applications, and allow the head to be held in place equally until the limb is reinforced and healthy. Then give the patient dry meat from a source free of moisture as long as the limb remains strong and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of making an incision is that you look at where the opening of the abscess is, and place the hot iron; for it is never in front; it's never behind; not to the right; nor to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, make the cut where the abscess opens, and place the hot iron, and perform the incision according to what you are able; and be careful not to damage an artery; watch for a flow of blood, so that the patient dies due to bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	On cautery of fire commands the diseased person to let their hair grow long and even; and if they poke at their origin, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone that a disease is called "catarrh" with the eyes or at the bottom, and this disease is old, and the medicine treatment does not help, then the last resort procedure should be the cautery, using which one would cut off the two major arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, you should cover the eyes. After that, let the patient lie on their back; rub the area with a coarse cloth until the arteries are visible. Then pull the diseased part of the neck to the entire length of one cloth. Next, observe where the vein lies and determine the position of each eye after the ears, ensuring they have returned to normal. Then mark both eyes with a cross, then cut each of them with an extremely sharp knife until the size reaches bone tissue, and do this by going across the width of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, pinch the pus near the artery and the vein above, cutting also as one inch through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, let the blood flow out continuously from high up.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery doesn't open upon touching, it is necessary to measure the length of the space of three inches and then cut until reaching the bone; what needs to be done with the blood that should be expelled is two-thirds (and by chance a bit more or less) according to what the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery. Then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone slightly, or if after incising we don't find the pus, then tighten the wound and bandage it, and apply ointment treatment until it heals.
de emigrainne	In the treatment of a fire cautery, instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and evenly; if they prick at their base, hold them still so they do not move until they fully grow.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	As the old age comes with and experiences acute inflammation and congestion, due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and lower back areas from past illnesses and similar issues; medicine treatment for these is done through methods of medical cure techniques. Yet, none of these treatments are effective, so we remove the arteries in the temples and apply fire cautery, as we have detailed.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method for extracting them is such that the patient feels behind their temples, and listens to the artery which opens up at the temple, as it opens well through its pulsation, and responds only in some people who are too cold; if it does respond, then cool the neck of certain cloths, then rub it with a rough cloth, and raise the head under hot water until the artery appears clearly. Then take the sponge that is shaped like this:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach an artery, then direct it upwards with forceps, and remove well all webs that are from each part; and if the artery is subtle, cut at the tip of the hook, then shape that section according to the amount of two joints. For if it's not cut properly, it will neither rupture nor pierce completely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And remove the blood from two to three; and if the artery is large, it should be tied with two threads of a strong silk thread, so that corruption does not occur in front of the healing of the wound, nor in subsequent bleeding; then cut off the excess between the two threads at this moment. And if you see, then apply the cautery gently until you reach the bone as long as the joints are cut; and this is the completed work, if the patient doesn't have fever and has warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	And the cauterization helps to finish off infections: because it provides more assistance against infections.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	In order for the removal of arteries, fill the area with old cotton and place it on well-made gauze; when you separate them, apply dry medicines that produce heat and gauze until they are clean; and should you cut into the artery as you work, quickly use a cautery or fill the area with vitriol and press your hand against it so that the wound is sealed; and if you do not have this present, place ice on the area instead until the wound is frozen, then rinse with cold water while keeping the wound from moving; and treat it as necessary. The one who moves faster during artery extraction when using a cautery should cauterize the blood vessel by cutting it in half across, but ensure that the cuts are deep enough to retain more of its heat for longer periods.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they retain less of their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And must have a gap of one large finger between the two knives, and then when you prepare to apply them both at once, and place the hot iron until it reaches the bone, and cut the blood vessel in two; and keep them apart from each other with the shoulder joints because there is no welding effect throughout this cautery technique; and this is how a cautery should be formed:
des larmes	Of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from veins above the testicle of the head of strength, and no medical remedy benefits, and you see the reddening action of the patient, and feel or front pulsation as if gasping; and at places they are tenacious and moist such that the hair of papers falls, and the papers heat up, and burn from the intensity of the tears, then it requires this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called the old one 'healing for injuries', and do this to the patient with this disease by making them let their hair or head, then I make three cuts across the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and make one cut as if two out along the forehead downwards until it reaches the nose tip, and the other ones two at each side above the papers, and be careful not to incise the arteries that are above the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and each wound should have three inches in depth perpendicular to the joins.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have ready a piece of sponge and some cloths to wipe off the blood, then pour in the quicksilver from two parts as it is shaped here:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made below the temple up to the second incision; and burn all the kerf that is between the two gaps throughout the entire sinus located above the bone. Then cut further along from the middle incision up to the other second, and then remove this pus-filled space.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If there is a tool placed in the first gap which is called 'cultellaire', and it has very sharp edges on one side, but not so on the other, it forms this:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cutting edge of the tool towards the fatty part in the kerf and the flat edge towards the bone. And insert the tool until it reaches the middle gap. And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision continues up to where the incision opens into the kerf, then cut further on the middle gap up to the other gap; and then drain the blood evenly, and pour out the pus; then place a piece of old cotton in each gap, and apply a moistened cloth with wine, oil, and saffron. And make sure that any abscesses do not appear. And on the third day, remove the stitches and apply a large amount of watered vinegar, then treat it with basilicon balm mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds, until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When there is a sudden onset of thick expectoration and you see the eyes withered and small, and weakening of vision, and burnt paper; and the hair falls out, and one sweats in fullness from fever, and the patient shivers, and the body is racked by fevers. Then know through these incidents that those substances and this mucus come from many veins, and the wet treatment applied, if it is correct, then this is how it should be.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you instruct the patient to look at their forehead again. Then make a large incision through the forehead, and another one wide. Now start from the left temple incision to the right temple incision, and ensure your cut goes until it reaches bone; and hold your hand away from the temples nerves that move during eating. And when the bone is revealed, drain all blood with an sponge. Then clean between the two lips of the incisions and insert old cotton wool and linen cloth; then cover with wet cloths soaked in wine and oil, making sure not to expose any abscesses; once the bone is removed, it's important you rub the bone until you see new tissue start forming, then apply desiccating substances that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of the wheat flower and four parts of comfrey, and make them into a paste; and apply it to these wounds to promote the healing of flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that passes through the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or mine stones or similar things like iron; or seeds such as beans, peas; or any flowing thing like water and air and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When they pass through the ear piercing or any other form of thing that does not fit with the ear and does not grow in the ear, you should expose the ear to sunlight. If you see the piercing, if you apply a few drops of violet oil or saffron oil, then proceed with extraction; and make them sneeze with consin (a type of ointment), when the sneezing comes, insert pieces of cloth or wool into the ear, and keep the ear above. Many times this cure works; and if it does not work to relieve pain, you should extract using fine tweezers, which is described as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps by force like pins, that's good; if not, proceed with the extraction using a fine needle of slight curvature; and if it doesn't jump through this, make an araneus (a type of tool used in surgery) and take hold of the head of the tool or the ear pinna firmly, and stick it into the waxed part of the tool until the wick cannot enter with the tool; then apply force with your hand as we have stated many times; and if force does not come out in this manner, grasp the tool at one end and take hold of its handle, place an instrument suitable for that task on either side, and insert a little cotton. Then press the wax firmly onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull with force.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump through all these things that we have said, then hurry to pierce the ear as though an abscess would burst from wax, and convulse. And the method of piercing is such that you first make a surgeon's incision in the tympanic membrane and drain blood according to its extent, then place the surgeon's hand between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and create a small incision at the base of the ear where the fat hangs down; and let the incision be as round as the moon until you reach the bone, then operate according to your ability, and suck it out quickly into your mouth; and treat with care when it is clean.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's granules that are inside and they are swelling, proceed with extraction; and if they cannot come out, proceed as follows:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And make an incision of that grain. But do not perform this when you think the grains are moist due to ear moisture, until you have done many pieces; then extract them with fine forceps and suction, as we said before, so that the extractions are clear.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In water then, if one vomits in the ear, let the patient use the discharge of cold water first, and fill up the ear with old cotton. And be standing next to that ear where the water is. If it splashes out through this method, it's good. If not, take many pieces according to their length and gently, then heat them slightly on fire; and place one or two of these inside her ear, and pull away from one foot from another part, and pull off with another piece from the piece that is in the ear; and do this continuously from piece to piece until all water comes out, and thus completely vomits. And if you see, take a small reed, and insert one of the shoulders into the ear, and the other shoulder in fire until the hottest part becomes charred; then redo several times until all water is expelled, as we said about the piece.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the beast, if it is small in size, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, perform the extraction with forceps; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from ears, when you treat it as we have said in division and dealing with distillations, if the treatment does not benefit, you must observe the ear to sunlight: if there is no worm opening, if you extract them using fine probes; and if nothing appears, take the form of this:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make the opening narrow at one end and wide at the other. And if they do not want to come out, stuff a cotton swab inside as I mentioned in the part about piercing stones; and if they still don't protrude like we said before, administer worm distillations that ancient people tested during worm extraction, and you will find it under treating distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, following the shape shown here as you can see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And make it of silver or an earthworm with two small holes at one end and a wide opening for distillation; and to press the essence within during distillation use one well-made araigne's tool fit for this purpose. If you see a rasp and wrap tightly around the tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the swab, and place that swab inside the ear; then stuff all the cotton into the rasp, press your hand gently until the oil is fully distilled or until the ear is filled; and sense the disease internally, and let the essence boil for a while when distilling it inside the ear; and make sure it isn't too cold because the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	On the cauterization of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a perforation in the ears; and this same thing happens to those who have ear injuries or dead bodies inside the ear. Such injuries occur none of them within the ear if it cannot be seen; and they do not appear twice to expel the perforation, yet one can see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And that which comes from within but cannot be seen is due to infection in various dispositions. And according to what you see, it is necessary for you to place the ear under the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent opilation, if the work has produced this pus of which I speak:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And cut and scrape all around front and back so it doesn't hurt the ear; if there's a thickening due to dead tissue or a bump on the ear, use sharp tweezers and gently pinch, until all the hard parts are removed.

Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor. de la char sor le neis	from the flesh near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans. quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose has been cut and sewn.

des apostemes des levres	from abscesses on the lips

de la char des gencives	from the flesh of the gums

des sordens	Of cauteries of fire command the ill to let their hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.

des apostemes de la gorge	extracting abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	No disease enters within the throat cavities that are called "godaths", and they're properly named as two almonds. When you treat them, just as we've explained in division, if they aren't healed, be careful: if these are pus-filled blisters small in size and with a white color, don’t touch them with metal at all. And if they’re red and the root is large, don’t touch them with metal either, due to blood discharge; but leave them until they're wounded, then you will remove them, or they might break by themselves; and if they are of pale color and have a thin root, prepare your tool for extraction, yet first check that these pus-filled blisters settle and calm down. Then make the patient face towards the sun, let their arms be in good health, and open their mouth while the surgeons press their tongue under all the tool, as depicted here; it should be of silver or finely crafted as knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the pus-filled blister? Take one and put it into the almond, then pull it upwards more than you can; remove nothing from the threads, then extract with the tool, as depicted here; it looks like a force. And both the head is placed upright, and one part after another are extremely sharp, and made of iron or silver.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool at hand, use tweezers instead, as depicted here:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make cuts on one side and the other name; and when you have performed one of the almonds, perform the other in the same manner, and after cutting gargle the patient with hot and cold water, as well as a gentle flow of blood occurs, then gargle with hot water or slices from cooked cherry tomatoes or laurel leaves, and similar things, until the saliva is fully cleansed; then continue the cure until it is healed; and no other abscesses are born in the throat than the two almonds, so perform them accordingly like the two almonds evenly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was born within her throat, namely a small abscess. I had almost completely sealed off the entire throat channel, so she could not breathe due to the obstructed passage and also could not eat or drink, dying if she remained in this state for one day or two. The abscess had ascended quite high, causing it to force out two tears through each of the two nostril holes from birth. I immediately acted quickly, put an ounce in one (of the nostrils), then pulled out the passage and a large portion of mucus; then made another cut near the other nostril hole, and had her open her mouth while pressing on her tongue; after that, inserted the ounce into this abscess, took out a part of it, and only came out with a little blood; and thus opened up the passage in her throat for the woman, started drinking water now and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at this abscess over a long period; and the abscesses were growing back immediately, filling the space that I had emptied until it became quite large; then I removed these parts, and only let God do what was left after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the head descends into the eye socket, and it is swollen and long, this is called "perpendicular"; and if it is out of place being large and round, then it's called "eye". When it is cured as we have said in division, and treatment doesn't improve, and you see that the abscess has calmed down and is subtle, then it should be handled; and this one which is round assembled and not long; and if it's bloody or of fusse color or black, then you should avoid making an incision into it. For there is great danger to the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner I said regarding its size and length, make the patient face the sun, press their tongue against the instrument we described previously; then insert the ounce into the eye, pull outwards from there, and cut it with two of the instruments that were mentioned in the division of the two almonds. And you should not cut more than the excess which is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms voice and speech; after the incision, use what was said about cutting into the two almonds, and treat until she's healed. And if the patient feels fear upon cutting, then you must apply a tool for cautery sensitivity. And the method of the cautery is sharp. And let the patient put their head back in your health, and then press their tongue against the instrument described or under the title of cautery, and clamp with living force; but not too thick nor too thin; and use the movement of this tool as it's formed:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let my head have a hair where I apply the medicine, like the movements of a spoon, and place the tool over all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient rest with their head on its side so that saliva and the mucus flow from their mouth to the medicine inside, but not down to the throat or causing pain; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see that it has dried and the effects of the medicine are reduced; and if you see this, take cotton and envelop it with any tool, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the tool on top of the cotton on wax, so that the cotton burns into the eye while it's damp; and do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for four to five days. And if you need to repeat the medicine cautery procedure, then do it again, after which clean around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and clean off anything left of the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargling until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or using the cautery; if it's treated with fumigation in this way, take calendula and ipecacuanha and oregano and rue and chamomile and lettuce and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them into one pot, put them there, and bring it to a boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot place two sticks according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be made of silver or sulfur, and until the vapor rises from the patient's mouth through their nose as long as the diseased womb is dead; after that you should repeat this often, until the womb dries out. Make sure not to do this at the beginning of pus expulsion when fever occurs, for many things can happen; instead, don't use this method during the decline of pus expulsion. And if this tool isn't available, take a reed and place an eggshell inside your mouth so that the diseased part doesn't get too hot; because the eggshell does not make the vapor weigh down on the mouth, it is a good combined remedy for salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, you may use the os or spine of a fish bone, with no need for anything else; if so, then it is suitable that you remove what you can see, and press your tongue against the sun on all the tool, until you see movement. For what cannot be seen opening in the throat, it's necessary to make the patient vomit out the diseased part so that the food becomes cooked in their stomach; if by chance this forceful expulsion fails to remove the disease; or if the disease swallows a piece of sponge, or belly button, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread; bind the sponge with thread and then swallow it. And when she comes to your mouth, you will see steam rise, and then proceed to force an expulsion; and if this doesn't come out from what we have mentioned, then take one tool shaped like lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And ensure the tools are adjusted near the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the head raised high; take care not to touch the epiglottis, letting nothing go through or pushing the bone inwards; instead guide the patient when they push the tool, as if they move or if something is too tight; should it be pushed down, or pull it forcefully with all the tool evenly, until she can do so.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No treatment is made with saliva alone, as I have described in the division by medicine cures; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the sick person towards the sun, and press their tongue with the tool that I told you. And if you see saliva, draw it out to about one small uncia or use fine tongs suitable for this purpose. If this doesn't work, take a hair, insert it in the throat toward the sickness, then apply pressure on its tip with heat like from a red iron and repeat often. And wet the sick person's mouth fully with cold water every day. Then wash their mouth open wide and let the water swallow slowly, and move their head often; and as soon as saliva feels the water, they will vomit it out.
