Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if she doesn't give birth as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the tool that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye. Do this multiple times, for she will not bleed without it. The method of fumigation is such: take one pot containing charcoal briquettes, cover it partially from inside with a perforated cover and place the tool's head inside its center. Then pour your fumigation into this, and hold the tip of the fumigator in her mouth, sealing it so no fumes escape but only reach up to the nostrils; and now the blood will come out. If she doesn't bleed, start the fumigation process multiple times again. Allow the patient to be thirsty, eat salty foods and alike, do not drink water; then she must leave her body in this manner.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used for bleeding, when it can be seen, resembles curved scissors meant to cut into the throat; and it has a similarity to the tip of a surgical scalpel, and it is sharpened like a rasp, so whatever she takes does not slip away; here's its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	No mention of abscesses are made according to what the memory brings forward from one and another in this book, and they differ both in perforation and in size; it is done in two ways where one is similar to its nature, and because it holds moisture. And the second way is for those that are on the body or they are within it. As abscesses at the head are different from those at the base, and abscesses at the fatty part of the head are different from those that come into joints, each has their judgement in operation.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And for abscesses, one should not pierce them until the body is dead according to its maturation. And if there are such that it's necessary to pierce when they have grown and do not mature as expected, like abscesses originating at joints. Because when abscesses originate at joints and are left until rotten inside by chance, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint become corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is within the main member, if you delay perforation until it's dead, it will harm the principal limb. Or if it is deep in the foundation, then piercing it so that it becomes dead; there should not be a situation where you pierce an immature, undigested abscess other than one that has become rotten from its base, and it grows into a fistula; and cannot heal within a large extent.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be known when the time for perforating an abscess that is dead according to its maturation, which is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and reduction of pain and flush, and the movement and firmness of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it should be ensured that you place the perforation site above the abscess or as closely as possible to where it opens outwards, and if the perforation is along the length of the body, and if the abscess is located at hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no crease.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those who bend, according to that limb. And when abscesses are within the fatty part of flesh, if you see them burst, let the puncturing continue until it is confirmed by digestion completion, as we have said. Because if you pierce before this confirmation, it might stretch across his body with venom from him and be full of heaps of filth; and might harden his lips and damage the parts beneath him. And for abscesses that are pierced along the width of his body, according to what the limb requires. And you must introduce small tools for smaller abscesses, small hooks; and in larger abscesses, large hooks, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it's necessary to use a knife, and cover them; when it has become as big as two cloths, and is numb, then do as you would with milking: and for those that split into three angles, and those that need to be covered like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses from angles; and for those where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar operations are done.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have none (of the tools), such as abscesses superficially situated, it is necessary that you pierce them completely; and when an abscess is large, and has accumulated a lot of pus, if you pierce but do not remove all the pus at once, but remove only part of it; then stop puncturing until the other side heals, then leave nothing untreated; perform this procedure by size in order from largest to smallest, until the pus exits entirely. Also, if someone's health is weak or a pregnant woman, young children, elderly and decrepit people. Because their spirits tremble with every release of pus, they might accidentally die due to it. Therefore, be cautious throughout this chapter, when you have pierced your abscess, if there is an opening, then check that the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a clean cut, use linen or old cotton for treatment; and if it's large and many hooks are used, each must have a tent so they face each other. And if you removed part of the skin in the abscess and sewed it back together, then fill it with old cotton or linen shreds without moisture, and secure it until the third day; then rest, and treat with ointment until healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your procedure, then treat with cold and ease, and moisten with a cloth for multiple times. And if the bleeding continues, then take control and treatment, and use the powders I mentioned in this book, and if it's in an area of water or if the skin around the abscess is very sensitive, then place wet tents and cloths soaked in wine and oil; and if it's in a solid area, and the skin is fatty, then apply moistened cloths soaked in water and oil, or wine and cold oil, until the third day as we have said; then remove and treat and cure properly, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to understand universally in the treatments of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here begins this chapter.
des soros	of the stones
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Or the chief brings out small abscesses, and their ways are like those found on a linen cloth, as with a goose's gallbladder, and many others share similar characteristics. There are some that are fatty and have moisture just like pustules; and there are others that are hard and stony when cut open, and there is no doubt that the artery would oppose it. And the operation of cutting involves using an instrument known as 'entromissoire', the form of which follows this description, containing something within it. For if it contains moisture, it is done from above to its length. And once the moisture is drained, it scalds without leaving anything behind in that containing the moisture; for it returns immediately when nothing is left there. Then dip cotton into Egyptian ointment if it's available; if not, use water and vinegar, apply it to the wound, and let it rest until another day; and this practice continues through the night. And then resume using the cotton as before on the second day, and the third, until you know that it doesn't stay overnight; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it heals properly.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the size above the abscess stones and moisture, it is lighter because there is little blood. And if in any of these abscesses or roots or there's no moisture, and of these two abscesses that I observed on the roots; and found the abscess just like a soft stone, rough and white, and unable to break; and if one had pierced through it, it would have been treated the same as a stone. In other abscesses coming or such as those that come from children's teeth and from ear canals, the opening is always for the longest possible time so that the pus can exit; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times there appear abscesses at the throat, and near the glands, and in angers, and not once come to other places or organs, they are soft and interwoven with each other. And each scrofula is properly within its node, like a nut and an abscess around a root, as we have said; and there are many appearances of these scrofulas. There are some that contain moisture, and others that do not want to obey treatment. In this one then that you see with good disposition towards the surgeon, and resembles the color of the chest, silent from every part and is not sensitive on either side of the neck nor artery nor conduit, and is not deep; it should be that you take it from above, and scrape off each part, and have both lips around the node if necessary, as we have said for abscesses around a root; handle them little by little, and make sure that you do not cut through the nerve or vein, nor make too much of an incision, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow cutting, place vitriol broil, or any powders that expel blood in the wound; and hold the wound until the abscesses are relieved and the wound is softened, then begins to putrefy. And when the blood has been expelled, return to your work until you finish it; then decide according to your skill if there are no small scabs remaining, remove and cleanse them. And if there's a large vein at the root of the scab, it should not be cut from its root but bind with a double strong thread, let it fall through this without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and proceed with treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you have cut the entire scab, it is necessary to assemble the two edges of the wound and stitch now. There should be no remaining excess due to the size of the scab. It's necessary to pay attention to cutting the root of this one, draining fluid, and stitching as we previously said. Those scabs that contain excess, pierce them where they open and drain; and do so in a similar manner as described before, depending on it, then apply bandages with ointment and other such things, until it is rottened by the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply ointment with flesh inside, until it's healed.
de squinance	regarding obliquity
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men spoke of how to make an incision in the throat; but I never saw anyone do it here, and this is written down from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squinting vision, it is necessary that the incision made in the throat which is called 'epiglottis' be avoided; and one should not offer aid by this method, because all the veins and the heart are close to the patient who has pus in their mouth or in the throat or between two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is within the channel of the heart, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to make an incision in the epiglottis, it is necessary that we make it through three circles or four with a small incision across, between the two circles. The size of the incision does not extend into the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these joints can be suitable for the sectioning of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessel is long from above.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary for them to extend the throat skin all the way down to the navel, then cut through the keor until they reach the neck; and avoid any blood vessels, if you see anything, and then shape the syfac, just as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the flow from the neck which jumps out through the limb that has been broken, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a period.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed where one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound as neatly as possible, and all the skin without the cartilage; then administer medicines that create flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis insists that one should not perform this until the throat is entirely blocked, and the patient is judged dead, and the defect is evident.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	So cut off the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe normally, and they are breathing through the wound, and this prevents death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And to command the old man to keep the wound open until the illness has passed, and it has passed after three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and treat it until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a maiden took one knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut some of the channels near the heart.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to treat her, and found her just as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found that blood was issuing from it, and indeed, there wasn't a cut or exit for the blood other than the throat, and the wind flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I acted quickly, treated the wound as it healed, and then I cured it until it was healed completely;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and there was nothing left for the maiden but to regain her voice which had been weakened by illness, and she returned after that to her usual state.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I swear that there should be no need for the surgery of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	From the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	Cysts known as "throat hernia" are often referred to, and they are large cysts in a dark purple color, and occur frequently in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And there are two ways: natural, and accidents; or natural does not have an organ.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents are according to two ways, of which one appears like fat in us, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us through an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there must be fear, and it doesn't suit to make cuts outside that in the one who is small, and the proof and search take place throughout the intervention:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as small as a nut, and cannot cut anywhere, then operate, just like one operates on nuts, and the treatment goes through all its stages, if there is any doubt;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And search well first, and treat it as appropriate until it becomes completely healed.
des nous	from now on
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many methods exist for us, so I will mention all similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And it is necessary that I tell all the differences between us and issues.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is characterized by heat and fever lasting until the body's secretions have passed and putrefaction has occurred; then, the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	In contrast to us, there is no heat or fever and no pain, it contains a pus of i syphilitic sac, which serves as its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a boil, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And according to two appearances, or greasy, or moist, and none of their colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treating the new, that you first test and inquire about all the instrument which is called 'intromissor', according to what its shape comes or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiring about abscesses among us is that you take or more moistened than what you find inside the abscess, and twist your fingers a little at a time, until you know that the instruments have pierced the pus, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the intromissor, and be careful not for it to jump.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	When moisture causes a problem, regardless of its nature or how it occurs, cut it just as I have instructed for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the incision no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, so cut it in an X shape and take it with tongs. Gently burn each side of it and place the piece where you found it back to ensure a clean extraction.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you can't remove it cleanly, remove it in parts so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything is left behind, it will recur to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it remains a little, and the patient doesn't suffer much, use some corrosive powders on the wound, and keep the wound clean, and place things that soothe and heal an abscess in hot water, and treat with other remedies until it's healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the wound is large, then stitch the two edges of the wound together, and treat the one who has been wounded with care.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is too close to be treated in opposition or otherwise if there's urgency, then use the site of vitriol juice and let it take its course for two or three days, as long as the wound heals, and rest with the boiling of blood; then return to coppering where some has remained from new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	These are the forms of the instruments for insertion, and they come in three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are four squares which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb". And among these there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, to surround the ulcers of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like needles that one removes from the spine, and made of citrine quartz, or iron, or silver, and yellow ones are valued for their use, and they are more adept at trapping black tar to seal abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the opening of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the lancets resemble sheep in appearance, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are pairs of lancets with two curves also, in three different ways.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And if there are lancets with two curves each, they also come in two ways; and if there are pairs of lancets with two curves each, and one-lancets with a single curve, all these come in two ways as well; and all this is necessary according to their size.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of this person to whom one makes the incision is sharp, and there are some who do not cut halfway but only from one side. We burn their cheeks because thus we do not cut into the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And for these introducers, their handles are put into gloves, so that the patient does not feel them during the opening of abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And there are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and only one should be used in the thigh area, such as legs, arms, and nipples, and similar body parts;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And no other small instrument once is made, resembling whips of surgeons, according to this shape, to which bleeding has been stopped:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed only once in the healthy part that closely divides veins and arteries, and not according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	No man's nipples ever swell when they begin to become corrupt, until they seem like female nipples;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them should do it according to this shape described in line B from b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strip off the fat, and apply medicinal ointment to the wound, then bring together the two edges of the wound for stitching, and continue treatment until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the belly sags down, and is flattened due to its size as in women, if they divide it into two sections above, by two similar cuts;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	From which one holds to the other at the end of each and both, so that the longer line contains the smaller according to this shape, from this line B until the line G;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then strip the skin that is between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply what we have instructed about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for treatment until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision has not been completed entirely, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood clotting, then you should fill the wound with wet cotton in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave him until he eats and regurgitates the meat and fat, then treat him until he is fully healed.
des apostemes des asselles	removal of abscesses and gallstones
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Wounds that occur from abscesses are manners of hard scrophulas, and if there are any containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those which contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from the line b until the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus inside the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment as needed until the wound heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses resemble smallpox, then cut them as we have said in cuts of smallpox, and if the wound is clean, then apply the cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	From the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	And when the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it heals over time, many times pus forms there. And similarly, this happens in veins with abscesses forming;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows that it's due to an artery, then the pus will be long and straight;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it with your hands, if you feel this squeezing sensation; and if it is through the vein, it will appear externalized.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it's foolish to deal with this abscess, and similarly when it is under the armpits and in the groins and around the neck and elsewhere, and it's quite large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	So one should avoid iron treatment, and also the one who is at the head, one should avoid this as well, and in the one who is swollen from an artery, do it over the skin until long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then work with the twelfth part, and remove the artery from the tissues, until it is fully exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then take out a needle from there, and pierce it up to the other side, and hold the artery in place with a double thread of two lews, just as I taught you in removing the two arteries that are found in temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then place the lever between the two threads with an introducer until the pus comes out which is there, and release the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then administer the treatment that draws off the pus, as long as the thread drains it.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then apply this ointment accompanying this, until it heals properly;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is due to the size of the vein, it's necessary that you color with your hand what part of the abscess you can reach on all the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then with the needle from the side you're holding in your hand, pierce it and leave two threads, so that you can pull them on the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie off the abscess, just as I have instructed you, or tie a stitch with two of the thread ends from each side of the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the child will endure pain, should you have difficulty with one needle made of all .1 filament throughout the entire abscess incision from the first needle's location, and hold the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut out the abscess as long as the excess goes out, then cut away the excess smoothly and leave that which is tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place a moistened linen cloth in wine and oil, then administer treatments of bandages and medications until they are healed.
des apostemes des ners	abcesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As with pus that comes into the artery and vein, pus enters the lungs when they are cut, or due to excessive labor, and similar occurrences.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often with shoulders and elbows and in all places that have joints, and it is one, pus filled abscesses, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and manifests in various positions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is squeezed, the patient feels pain, and does not fully match the sensation of flesh but rather within the gut;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And moves in all directions, neither going forward nor backward, neither above nor below, and that which is located at joints does not fit well under iron: by chance it would cause constriction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And the one who is a head or forehead, causes the skin to blister.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the boils are small, and you have some forceps, grip them at their base;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they are large, lift them at their root, and cauterize them, then cut the flesh, and suture the wound together, and continue treatment until it heals properly.
des grosses boces pendans	Large boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	No instance occurs in wombs or any other part like this, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by its appearance, and has a subtle root, and large knots; and there are both small and many large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw one person who had two bellies that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, they were white, and had a small root, and were cut open, and were corroded by moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I dissected them and found that in one there were 16 ounces weighing, and in the other 5. The organs at incision show that when you look, the patient's body is moist, and the color of the fungi is white and moist with a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If it is large and full of pus, then let the fire cautery be at your disposal. For the surgeon often experiences too many blood losses during operations, and if you are absent, then quickly take up the task of applying heat treatment;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	And if you see the patient frightened and fearful from the incision by the iron, then take a well-made piece of hemp string, and tie it in a knot as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	And then keep pulling it tight, and do not cease to pull the hemp string until you reach the knot, and feel no strain; and if the roots are thick, then feel frightened even for the belly, but you should be able to cut half of them.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then apply heat treatment so that it does not heal prematurely; then treat the wound, and make sure you do not cut into the tender tissue which is of a red color and has little sensation and produces pus.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess, and I will come to the treatment of gangrene next.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the bile flows freely
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	When the appearance of bile comes from a surgical wound or a cut in the stomach and is found on some parts of the intestines, just like it happens in other cuts, or blood that escapes from veins or arteries as per its position, or due to windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it's from the cut in the stomach and by the outlet of the intestines, then its color is similar to that of a pus-filled lesion, and it is a slight matter without much pain, opening from various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the passage of an intestinal obstruction, then it is more varied, and when one presses it with their fingers if it returns, and then comes back, and by chance if it gets stuck, and expands quite a bit at the entrance during bathing and due to strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it's a simple matter and opens well when you press it with your hand, it doesn't get stuck; and if it is due to blood, it will open through these signs large and hard pus blisters, and are located according to the amount.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to wind (or风气), you feel suffocation at the throat, and the veins so that you observe whether their appearance resembles blood from an artery, or a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	If you must leave the treatment alone. For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in chapter on abscesses, concerning arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if it appears to be near the intestine or the bowel, then you must instruct the patient to bleed his liver and ensure that he lies fully straight, then pierce through all around the belly;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then instruct them to lie with their body between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	Then go straight to the area where you marked on all parts of the body,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then cut half of the abscess above each major curve;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	next tie it firmly around with a strong thread or a sturdy silk cord, and bind it tightly until the abscess is fully resolved;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then cut half of the abscess laid out over the binding, and place your index finger in it, and examine the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it has been tied up by the bellybutton, release it, and push the intestines forward beyond the stomach.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you come across the kidney, take hold of it at the root, and remove the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if it goes against the artery or vein, go straight down through them and then come back to your task; take two needles and push out two long threads, and place these two needles inside where you pierced in a cross pattern.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then pull the abscess up with four fingers on top of the needles and if you see anything, remove the needles; let the wound heal on its own until it dries, and bury the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	When it becomes subtle and solid, then you should treat according to what is needed, and incise the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And remove the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound according to what is needed, and sew the wound.
dou chancre	and the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed the appearances of the ulcer and how to handle it with medicines, and how to avoid iron treatment; let us speak of the ulcer that is in the marrow, and there is great caution needed in its treatment, as the ancients said. If the ulcer is in a place where you can scrape it out, like one on the breast or in cooking utensils, and other similar places, then you should remove it entirely when it's just starting; but if it's large and old, don't attempt to touch it, because I have never known anyone to recover from such ulcers; no one ever recovers from them in front of me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the works, when it is in place or can be taken out, as we have said, you must purge the patient of black bile only once; then let a surgeon treat him if he shows signs of fullness, then remove the black bile to where it needs to be for surgery. Then wash your hands and hair thoroughly everywhere without leaving anything behind; and let bleeding occur completely while you keep pressure on the area with your hand or nothing else, and if the bleeding goes against the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize until the wound is cleaned; then treat it again until he heals.
de ydropisie	Regarding dropsy (edema)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have discussed the appearances of dropsy in division, and how this water assembly is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the treatment that is done with medicines, and that which is treated with iron: it only refers to these two; and should one not use iron in these two conditions: these being tympanites and yposarche, because they are deadly things; therefore when you treat this dropsy appearance called 'dropsy' with medicine, and if the disease doesn't improve with treatment, then check if the patient's condition is weak or if he has any other disease apart from dropsy, such as abdominal distention and similar conditions; if iron should not be used in these cases because there might still be doubt; and when you see that the patient is very pale and has no other disease apart from dropsy, and isn't too young nor too old, then you can proceed:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient straight up with your hands, and have them press their belly as they drink water at the lowest part of their foot. Then take the thorny spike according to this form: And make it 2 inches long at a pointy end, but do not make it so deep that when you insert it, it cannot reach until inside the intestines upon insertion, and cannot be pulled out;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look to see if the dropysis is beginning near the intestines: if it seems that you need to cut through in this area about 3 inches from below the belly button; and if the dropysis is due to liver disease, then make your cut on the left side of the belly button at three inches. And if it's due to gallstones, then do it on the right, and it must not let the patient lie on the cut where excesses might flow into that weak spot.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the tool and pull it out, lifting your hand to place the thorny spike between the skin and flesh as you would scorch at the size of a fingernail or around that; then pierce the flesh until the thorny spike reaches up to about an inch from the top, this is the width of water, then remove this tool which has been described in detail. It resembles a thin silver cane, made of iron or brass and is light in weight, with one small point on each side; on one side, there are three points; and on the other side, another point and again on another side; and you shape the shoulder as if it were a feather, this is the form of incision that writers describe when they carve out feathers.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top is the liver, so that when the instruments come to the water, they now descend on the instrument; empty it then either half or one third, for if you empty more than it should in this hour, by chance the patient might die from the release of his spirit due to the weapon's action, or he could faint, or he approaches death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the virtues indicate in the patient, and their pulse; then move the instrument and hold back the water, and it is held now for the anesthesia which numbs the pertus that is on the syphilitic lesion, as I have spoken about, that you pierce this way; then begin using the instrument again another day, if you see the patient suffering from this one, and draw a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this each day, and refrain from drinking as long as there is no remaining but a little of the water. And if you doubt about the patient, leaving more water, if the treatment for burial or sand becomes hot, and by much sweating or bath and in sunlight, and if it stains with drinking; and treat with drying medicines until he has recovered, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after removing the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Regarding the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	No child is born without having testicles in the penis, or if they are small, or if they do not occupy their proper place. If it happens that he has to pierce through all .i. very fine spatumile according to this form: then put one .i. very thin clo of plonc and tie it and keep it like that for .iij. days or iiij. days, and when it wants to urinate, if you remove the clo, it will urinate, and then you put it back again; and perhaps this does not happen because the urine that comes out does not leave the clo closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the testicles are small, if they use a plonc clo medicine, as we said before, it will enlarge. Those who do not have their testicles in their proper place are blind, because no one is born with testicles at the tip of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot conceive either due to the matter being unable to reach the prostate, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way to do this is for the patient to lay on his back, then lift the head of the penis and the scrotum as well as large as a feather's tip, so that the bits are spread out in the middle, just like it should be; and beware of bleeding which occurs many times, and if it happens, stop it with the one who stops blood flow, and treat the wound until it heals.
