si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so that you can consider the instrument you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The joints hurt either from within, or from outside;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have treated that corrosion by the application of medicines, and if they do not benefit at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	So it is necessary to cover that limb up to the joint where the corrosion occurs,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the disease does not escape through death, or through malice, which is greater, from the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	And these are its signs; if the limb becomes black, as though it has been burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness comes this decay spreading from member to member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	it spreads throughout the body; if you hasten with copper,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it's due to the impact of certain venomous beasts, such as sea spiders and snakes, etc.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corrosion is at the head of the two, then treat it, and do not give it space to come up until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if you treat at the joint, so that the corrosion does not extend up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it goes up to the arm, if you treat with a knife; and if it passes the knife, then it's death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	It is not for remedies beyond that of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And similarly do so when the corrosion comes or piece: if it comes in the first joint, then treat after another joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes or piece, then treat the entire piece;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it ascends to the leg, then treat at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes above the knee, if there is nothing else than for the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the method for covering or sewing a limb is such that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one finger with one of the threads down, and another finger with the other thread up,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you open the flesh that is between the two threads to one inch wide, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then you sew or use silk, and place one inch strips of linen from each side, so that the thread does not touch the healthy limb,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And to the patient brings another injury and abscess to the feet.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And when blood flow starts as you work, if you quickly cauterize the wound,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some restraining powders; then return to your remedies until the treatment is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured limb with a reliable bandage and treat it until it heals properly;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you about what happened at one house during my time.
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	It had a blackness that seemed like the certainty of fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	And that corrosion came first to his two feet, until it consumed all of his foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the patient saw the corrosion, they immediately sought to cover their feet, and were saved.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And long after this happened, I experienced a burning sensation in my hand, and it came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And I began applying counteracting treatments after the purification of the body, yet could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to apply my hand to it, but I refused, hoping for a reaction from the substance;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	For the strength of his spirit was weak; and he became despondent everywhere, and returned to his homeland.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he raised his hands in desperation, and became sane (possibly meaning he came to a state of clarity or sanity).
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have only shared this so that one might perform another part if needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No abscess ever comes in the inner flesh, and stays for such a long time as to cause a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then cut and stab, and have the arrow jump out, and remain with the man's eyes, just like some vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the leather that is above is also as thin as one eighth of a cloth thread.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	And they do not reach up to the bone or nerve, and such diseases are called "blind".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And it is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it's so extended that it comes up to the bone exactly, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And in the cooking process, if you peel that skin all over, and similarly when it's delicate, like a piece of fabric;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and doesn't swell because of its putrefaction.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have made the skin burn and the corruption hasn't reached exactly,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And the skin is thick with flesh, if he treats a catarrh like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look if his breasts are large, and his belly that contains them has a bad smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then administer an Egyptian cathartic medicine like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take ash, oil, and litharge, in equal amounts, and cook them together in a single pot on the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	While the medicine remains red, and thickens as much as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	And then take of this according to your need, and prepare it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and apply it inside the stomach, and keep the body constrained;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	let the medicine remain for 2 hours, then extract it by rubbing;

Des vils	Of low origin
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Their veins are thick, wavy vessels filled with superfluous melancholic substances, which affect many body parts.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more often occurs in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry things, compared to others.

Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The bathing process is as follows: immerse the first leg in very hot water for a long time until the large vein becomes thin.

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "Bovine Illness", because it often affects the cows,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and a small worm is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body going up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it can be felt all over the body when you touch limb by limb, until it reaches the skin where it went, and jumps forth;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And is infected with pus from certain fluids, if snakes and worms and roundworms or pinworms come near the abdomen;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And there is doubt about its illness, for when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance it enters, and destroys the eye; this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and drained, one can only wonder as to when it will end:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So then, it is necessary for you to tie the arm above and below with a strong bandage very tightly,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then cut upwards and pull forcefully, and if it is correctly aligned in the flesh, you won't find it,

et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greater discomforts that it causes, are when it goes to the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it approaching or its head near the eye, hold steady over it with both hands, then lift up, and apply force.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	It is necessary to use the application of purgative remedies for ailments caused by humoral disorders,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And if there is corruption in meat due to rot.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it's a pain that comes to any limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and spreads from member to member; and I have seen what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was summoned to help a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, where I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and about an inch later, it rose up as high as a worm on its shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	Sooner than any other thing, just like quicksilver when it is cut off from another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain leaves the affected area and enters the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little later spread throughout the entire body, until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I noticed that it was spreading within the body as well, just like when I observed it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was marveling greatly how she moved from member to member in such a way, for I had never witnessed this disease in such manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I have seen many times that well often moved pain from one limb to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never experienced it myself, as I see in the case of a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was because women have a wet body and their veins are exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And through this appears that constrained wind;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not become evident according to this reason in those who are delicious, and have moist bodies and responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the treatment of this disease, and if the patients feel pain, if it appears to you in the way we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the wound opens up and down quickly, and then stops until that constrained wind at the body comes out;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	And apply the cautery to the area; and if you cannot see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the treatment for those who dislocate the windpipe, such as stinking pills and pills of sarapin, and similar others.
Des saiettes	From arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and spiny, and soldered;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one that urinates in no member but does so according to two ways: or in the main member, it streams,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or like the brain, heart, liver, kidneys, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it happens then, indeed, at no place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, becomes apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	it must be that you are cautious about the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in various conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when that bad sign does not appear and the arrow has not fully exited, then remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow penetrates through bone and strikes the fluid reservoir above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	When there is a surgical incision and tension and swelling around it, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and confusion in understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes affects the nose or ears; and sometimes impairs speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is moisture around the wound that appears white like pus, and it also seems burned like charcoal.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign is seen, hold on to the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it's still there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it exits or pierces through the heart is that it's close to the left breast, and also feels as if it has been stuck into something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the arrow also moves like a pulse, and there is black blood, and coldness comes with cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, without doubt, know that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never pierces is that bubbles do not jump out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly with coldness.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow stops in the thigh's covering, it pierces the small bones; and causes great pain and severe suffering and sighing; and moves all limbs from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow stops in or near the stomach, by chance it jumps out of the wound with any undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow stops in or near the stomach or abdomen, and it jumps out without any meat passing through the intestine, there is no hope for treatment, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow stops in the bladder, and the urine jumps out, causing severe pain for the patient: you should know that this wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and the neck and the throat and the shoulder blade and the auxiliary (shoulder) bone and the spine in the back and the ribcage and the hip bones and the legs, and resembling limbs, are protected according to many arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it's not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because when you do something else.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened at one hour that an arrow hit him on the breast near the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and conducted it from there through the fat of the ear, and was without serious harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And try to pull an arrow out of a game where it has fallen into the oil grease underneath the paper underneath,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow had been returned, yet one could only reach its tip towards the shaft,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, having a weight of only one feather without any bells; the game was healthy, and it did not come to any bad accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And try pulling an arrow from the neck of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with bells:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	Cutting the beard, and trimming it as I moved along, left the Christians clean.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And extracted an arrow for about one inch, where it was in the back or belly, and I thought it would kill him;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And then after he had passed thirty days, if his position did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and set it up, and pulled it out forcefully, and there was no bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see one arrow that falls or hits, and there is a wound stitched together;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and lets the arrow remain inside, without changing its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor does it find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And observe another person who was hit by an arrow on their face and the wound has been stitched shut;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And thus he stays suffering great pain; and no other similar phenomena.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And took an arrow from one hundred to the king's bodyguards that was embedded in his left side,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was leaning slightly towards the right side; and the arrow was fully inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat the wound after it had been embedded for three days. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I pursued her all with subtle attempts, and did not feel her;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he would feel a burn and pain around his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of the arrow causing this.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on a plaster that helps in healing and digestion for the sake of the ear not swelling;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the healing ointment for days, and quickly resolved the wound, and so I let the afflicted person rest long enough.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	Until he felt the arrow within his nose; and he told me that.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive aqua regia medicine to the wound for days until it was opened up,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	And I tried, and felt the tip of the arrow which was penetrating at its base;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted during the opening of the wound through that medicinal agent, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and pierced deeply into the inner parts for three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then I eased it out so that I could grip the tip with my forceps, and pulled from both sides, but couldn't remove it;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore never stop refining and designing ways to construct instruments, until I had one day made good pliers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Following this manner towards the end of this chapter, as long as I continue to do so and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And those who judge believe that the cartilage under the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I would then heal it, and the wound was joined, and the patient's health was completely restored.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	You have been told about the quality of extracting certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you apply your method to what I do not say, for books cannot take in everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but listen to my master brothers on a few important matters, and those that are current and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	prove nine works, and the ninth instrument, for the expulsion of foreign things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come from any part of the body where they are stuck, according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by their head where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And the one that jumps out or enters at its head is an arrow entering the body's flesh, and it jumps out only once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump out now, let her stay until the body is cooked internally, and wait for its release;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And even if it's embedded in the bone, and it cannot come out, if you leave it like this for several days, and remove a little each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it breaks out, and if it does not break out, if you pierce through with a thin needle all the way until the bone is broadened, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is embedded in the head bone, and goes up to one of the brain chambers,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and none of the accidents that I have described appear to the patient: if you do not remove it, but let it remain until it becomes equal after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow reaches up to the heart, then it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow only pierces into the bone and does not reach up to the heart,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient experiences no bad accidents for several days, if the wound is properly treated.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's firmly stuck in that way and cannot come out by itself, then you should apply arrows internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals properly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to its place within the body so that it cannot be seen, then one should seek for it with all their might.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then try to guide it with any suitable tool;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot find it due to the constriction of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve or vein, so you make it as large as possible;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and try to pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears attached to where it is lodged,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the bone sticks out from two parts at its tip that you can push,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	do so carefully to ensure that you do not break the arrow and make its removal more painful.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it in one attempt, until the shoulder is properly aligned within its socket, then move it. For the extraction process is made easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the blood flow is against what it should be, then follow what we have said about treatment in our chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against the incision near the nerve and vein, and use skill to pull out arrows without risk,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or gently, either firmly or moderately; and place the patient according to their form when they were hit by the arrow,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for this is the greatest help that it can be, and if you cannot do so, then lay him according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, or if there is no sign of it in the body, or if the skin is swollen at a place where you can see or feel it obviously:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Thus raise up high, as long as the tongs can seize, and then grasp: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it's held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it can't come out, leave it still, and then start the extraction again until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it's from the arrowhead that is stuck in him, push it all along the shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it is closed, and you see the administration of a hot application, then administer one tool heated,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	and when the tip of the arrow enters the hair of the tool; and then apply force,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is hooked [in], then I use one pointed tool to enter in [the wound], for easing the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you remove all the flesh around or where the wound enters, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if an arrow enters or pierces the chest or abdomen or bladder or rib area, and it is close to vital organs, you should cover it immediately, assuming one can do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware not to cover the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and afterwards suture the wound; this is a task that requires skill.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat the wound until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used for extracting arrows resemble an eagle's beak, and here is how it looks:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in various sizes: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the arrow's tip is also like a bird's feather,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	so that it can pierce at the tip of the arrow, as shown by this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers to use for pressing and extracting is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins similar to those common ones
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which we cleanse are thirty-one, of which there is a head of sixteen.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means to say: two small ones that come after the ears, which are called 'the sweet herbs';
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the two arteries which are in the two temples visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, which are called 'whisks';
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is within the forehead; and the vein that is on the head below the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins that are above the mouth on the lips, and these veins are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And the two veins that are along the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins we usually treat are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it runs along the left rib, and they call it "the head vein";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the main is called "blench", and composed of the cephalic and the basilica,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call them the lay people "vein near the heart"; and the basilica is either on the left side or on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they call them the lay people "vein near the belly", and it's above the flanks.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And this is the one that heals, which opens clearly over the abdomen.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the veins are the ones between the thump and ring finger, and if you have two of them;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and at the ankle there are three veins: one is below the bend of the pocket on the left side of the body,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second is deep one which is on the anklebone on the right side of the body; and the vein that is called "the knee", it is in the anklebone on the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The care for veins located behind the ears is something the ancient cathartics helped with, and also for migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of a surgeon, as I've told you, and that you release the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the neck where the veins are with a rough cloth; then pinch the neck's opening tightly with your fingers.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	Until you can see both two veins protruding behind the ears in two loops dependent from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Guide them to your side, and where you feel the pulse on your side, if you know how to listen;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the scalpel, and press it along the vein towards the bone, then lift your hand all up to the vein upstream;
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and remove the skin and the vein well two inches through, and let blood flow out until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then tighten and hold [the wound] tight, until it heals;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken of incision and cauterization, or first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is akin to ancient inflammation,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and also, and habitual eye pain, and in the body of the weeping fever's eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of the surgeon is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is because the patient pulls their neck, until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the hair under your hand, and then declares they've found something;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lifts the skin over the vein at the top of your hand near your index finger, and holds the scalpel there;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lifts the vein at the top, and cut it, just like you did with other veins, and do whatever is necessary according to the amount of blood needed;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place it on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then have the veins healed and leave them until they are cured; and we have spoken about this and their extraction, or where to begin with the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment for the veins of the forehead is just as valuable as that for the occipital veins in treating ancient diseases of the face, and migraines, and redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient tightens his throat by twisting it, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the tool which is called "cautere", as described below:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and apply force with your hand or something else, and allow a small amount of blood to flow according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then relieve the patient of their collar, and tie the vein until it is tight and healthy, ensuring there are no slippage or wide openings.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	For any vein, it is not proper for the flames to be too close or large; and the healthy tissue should run across rather than down, because the bone is near, and by chance the flames could break when they are delicate.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the nostrils serves the eyes, and the nose, and the reddening, and at the ear inside the eye, and diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their healing is that the patient twists their neck by tightening a certain ligament, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it, and let the healing pass through, a bit long like the flame, a little wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is thin, perchance it breaks; then make it correspond to blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The treatment of a neck injury near the nose involves an incision, and is separate from surgery, and also deals with diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If it's like migraines or reddening that comes to the face, and similarly when she becomes old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the quality of this treatment is such that the patient narrows their throat, then presses their nose to your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And take the slender flame long, and insert it into the lip at the space which is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open properly and the wound is now beginning to heal;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and does not progress too quickly below the wound, and let it bleed gently according to your need, then give her a night, for she is very soon restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the two kidneys helps with narrowing of the arteries, and the beginning of infectious diseases, and many illnesses, and in congestion, and corrosion, and herpes, and abscesses;

et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And may it be that the master stands above the head of the patient, and the patient lies down on his side,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then let the blood vessel be opened long but a little wide, then drain off the blood gradually, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then sew it up in the other vein, then release the tie, and partially restrain the blood vessels.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	That the sick person is not strangled; and let them stay until morning, so that the wound heals.
De la sainie des leivres	About the surgery of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The surgery for veins above affects the mouth and causes gum decay, and cuts in lips, and nosebleeds and inner cheeks.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of this surgery is to have the sick person sit in front of you, and restrain their neck as I've explained;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the mouth, and look at these two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And one knows them by their being black, and by the fact that inside they have small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	So then handle both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you take the largest of each part, and do exactly the same with the two veins that are above and below, because it's the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the cure around the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The cure around the veins that are below the tongue aids after the treatment of the head, and this is done near the throat, and for diseases of the lymph nodes, and for diseases in the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the skill of the healer is that when the patient's condition improves in your hands under the sun, and you lift their tongue, and look underneath on each side, there appears a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then heal both of them, and do not overdo the treatment, because near the arteries they are.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins in the arm that we commonly heal are treated according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	They are cauterized either by applying one large hot flame, or by using a subtle olive oil if they resemble the veins of a butcher's knife, and these are called 'anise'.
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And their width and fineness correspond to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is greatly esteemed, and it appears wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And one must open the veins filled with large visible blood, and those containing large blood and disturbance;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the shape of the olive-flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle and pointed; for it aids in cleansing the fine veins or has delicate yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The healing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that affect the throat, and the neck, and the abdomen,
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it's fitting for the surgeon to heal carefully, and he should be aware of the artery that is there.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it cuts the artery, and bleeding occurs, then it's fitting to staunch the bleeding; as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And it should not be held by the flame, but cut so like a hare.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if it is not clearly seen when the basilic vein opens, then you must extract it and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	You want no pain from this, or you sever the vein instead of it in the arm: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cover the wound with a bandage before, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know how to find the location of the wound, then it is appropriate that you straighten the arm, touching the place until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the place of the elbow, and then bind the arm, and cut open with the flame cautery before it.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful not to cut into the artery when you see the elbow inflamed, for that is where the artery is: listen out for it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding up like the urine of a child, and the veins are red and fine, know that these are veins from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	So hurry up, place your finger for a long time, then remove your finger when it has stopped bleeding, as this happens many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Tie the arm down, and leave it like this, and do not move the patient's limbs; place them under fear, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and it takes time, and the medicine is unavailable for you, if you must open an artery when it appears, because the head of the wound retreats; stop the bleeding on the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark from a willow tree, and cut it, and take one of the halves and bind it tightly until the other side.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound stops bleeding, that's good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop the bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the dressing is not chosen among many preparations because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's joint.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of the vein in its middle is helped by treatment that reduces blood flow from above and below, and
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	Because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is important for the surgeon to be cautious when operating on it because there is a nerve beneath, and if he doesn't go far enough down, and he finds the nerve;
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it inflates and health is harmed, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any places due to its subtlety, then it is necessary for you to have the organ removed before. And listen carefully as you feel with your finger.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The treatment of the forehead helps, since it leads blood to the head, and assists with pain;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to treat by fire with olive oil or by the fire of myrtle, for this is the safest of all veins because there is neither injury to the nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	In every case, it's best to seek the lightest touch and not be discouraged if one fails the first time, and then try again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And perhaps some limbs swell in certain individuals even when one tries for the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of treatment depends on your thought or consideration.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about healing, it is that healing should be practiced only to preserve health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the healing be done in one of the three veins that are or cut: this means, the cephalic vein, the femoral vein, and the basilic vein;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And it is necessary to start fasting when prayers are recited at the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and after meals during winter, when the sign of fullness becomes evident;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And it is necessary to fast on the first or third day, after four hours or five days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	Fasting for the treatment of diseases does not have a specific time limit, but it is done according to need on any day or at any time;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And fasting should not be applied to children up until the age of twelve years, nor to a woman pregnant for only a quarter of her pregnancy duration until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	No one who has surpassed sixty years of age should undergo surgery.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wishes to be healed in any way, if it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a gentle catheter,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has retained some urine, so that the veins do not draw off the unnecessary substances harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	No one should be healed if they are too full of meat, or if they are drunk, even if they have strength, or if they have dropsy;

puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the bodily fluids. If they are abundant, due to meats and beverages and medications, if you have the means;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then take a bath, if no obstruction exists, to refine the blood,

et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And tie yourself tightly and joinably, and let the heal be higher than where it is being healed, and rub the arm twice or three times.

puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the wick of a small amount of old oil, then place her duty of her left hand on that vein directly above his shoulder a bit or where she wants to ignite.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burn and break due to being pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	Because there are veins that behave like strings when ignited, and some of them are filled with windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	meaning that when you place them over the flame, they draw towards the flame and cannot open the vein, resulting in one being among those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, because in these matters the surgeons need to be knowledgeable.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it's good; and if not, it should be tried again slightly near that place or on the skin quickly, when the limbs are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the body fluids are escaping, then it should be left for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	In case there are pus-filled blisters, do not enter or bathe in water; then try to clean again if it suits.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the artery is small, or the vein slightly more difficult to identify and you doubt that there isn't as much blood leaving as you see, so pierce it directly within that very same artery all the way through.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And work a little hastily, so that the veins swell up; for this happens often, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the vein swelling, do not restart the treatment immediately, and place a little oil on it, for it eases the body of blood, and heals in this area where the oil is.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And apply the oil when you are treating each vein treatment, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same thing happens with treacle and wax when you place them on the ear; their subtlety is such that they expand if they are too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And when it comes to large abscesses that often occur, this happens even if the person has not been able to bleed enough times or if the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you are in haste, soak an earthen sponge with water and a little warm wine, and keep it on the ear for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	It is necessary that you do this after the bleeding from the vein, and if it remains in the ear for several days without any darkening or discoloration, then it does not harm it;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see it, place on any thing of aloes or of myrrh dissolved in the juice of calamus, monster, or alike.

Des sainies de ventouse	Extracting the blood with suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or spiders, or leeches; and blood extraction is done in two ways: by piercing and drawing out blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction cup method that involves piercing is done in two ways: either hot or not using heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	Blood extraction through puncturing and blood removal is performed over the course of twelve months in three quarters of a year,;
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	Because one is completely around the head; and the other is inside the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And the other two are in both sides of the neck; and the windpipe under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the windpipe above both shoulders; and the windpipe at the armpits;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the windpipes inside both arms; and the windpipes in both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the suction cups on the two ankles; and suction therapy does not treat blood, for it deals with small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And because of this, one doesn't weaken oneself, as one does in the practice of bloodletting;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, nor at any fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from excess, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of the diseases suction is needed, or as a habit, if we administer it every hour at the beginning of her period, or at the end, and during and in each interval;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they have the need to perform suction, if they weigh heavily on the head;

The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: you should place it first in a state of being empty, and apply steady sucking pressure, and position it quickly, moving it evenly, and keep doing this until you see the area turn red and swell up, then stop when you perceive the color of blood; then remove it, and reapply the suction cups, and take care regarding the disposition of the body parts. Indeed, there are some with thick skin and clear pores: for these, it suffices to pierce once, and create wide wounds, with a bit of depth; and suck lightly.
