et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is only done for the purpose of drawing blood from limb to limb,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	if like we place them on the nipples when the nose is bleeding; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, or like we place suction cups on the stomach and intestines to reduce the size of the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And when there is pain due to an obstruction or stone, if it attracts the obstruction by its attractive power, or removes the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus it acts when placed over the heart and lungs where there is a retained wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these suction cups are applied empty solely for the extraction of fluid; and they are never used combined with fire, nor filled with warm water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	In diseases like pleurisy, and in such manner one would fill the suction cup with hot water, or with water that has cooked medicinal herbs useful for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup used for fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And have two and a half palms in length by width, and has or lacks at its middle one small notch, as to pierce an awl,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and let it be made of iron, so that when it is placed on the body, it does not burn the skin;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a rod across from iron or aragonite, so as to put a candle holder on it.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And let them be large or small according to the illnesses and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suction cups for children are different from those for adults, and those that are skinny compared to those that are fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must place this suction cup on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take a wax plug or one line of thread and put it inside the suction cup, then insert the end of the thread through the penis which is inside the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	If the clarity of the suction cup is at the bottom, so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it on the same limb, and you should either at the spot we have mentioned, so when desired, if the vapor goes along with the suction cup, remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And apply the lotion in the same way as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, there should be neither a ridge nor any part at all, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and placed on the limb merely;
et c’est li forme:	And it's this form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without suction cups are used only in limbs where one cannot put suction cups because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on the naked areas of meat cuts, like a pig's foot or a dog's, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And when you find veins that are clear and sweet water without pus, if you take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and immerse them in sweet water until they are familiarized, and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then bleed and apply suction cup medicine until the limb turns red, and place them on the veins.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and bleeding, if it's possible to place a suction cup, do so, because that is much better afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the limb with ease, then water, quite well, and then incision;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb is raised too soon after the body of the abscesses, get wet. Take one and a half yards of linen in cold water, and place it on, until the abscesses are hardened;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are multiple abscesses, then put on ground glass or garlic and similar items until they harden;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you place half of peeled beans on the limb, and let them dry on the limb until they stop bleeding now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more expertise, take other instructions.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the veins are not to be taken easily, rub with a fresh blood clot or insert an awl until blood starts flowing.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then place them, and as soon as they feel the flow of blood, they should start working;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are bleeding, apply a little aloes and ground oatmeal or ash on them; now they should start healing.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and for restoring fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear son, that the leaves of this chapter were scattered from it, so no one saw any of the old books or read a letter.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the knowledge has been removed from our land, because I never found anyone good in it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, for by the knowledge of old books, or from which I have studied so much that I dealt with this science, and through experience, and through the custom of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained, and abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we outline or introduce this book's contents and chapters where the senses apply their understanding, staying true to reality. This way, those who have experienced it will know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twists or sprains occur to any part of the body, it is necessary that you quickly treat the patient from one side and then the other, without causing anything else to happen. This includes things like weakness, children, or elderly people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the place where you're holding is too tight, or too cold; and eating cold foods, that means cold meats, and liver and buckthorn, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill on meat which fills veins with blood, until you have doubt about pus formation in an abscess, or leakage of substance from the body part; if the patient begins to feel better after your initial treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with meats that cause abundant nourishment, or have a viscous quality, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and chestnuts, and peas, and beef stomachs, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, among similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with this nourishment, the injuries are healed more quickly and the breaking [of bones] is overcome.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken in old and weak people cannot be healed or sutured according to their nature due to the drying of the limbs, nor those also which are too tender, such as children's bones;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but do not hesitate, reset the broken bone. With large thorns which pierce and unite the limb together, until it is as strong as before; and do not finish his work too quickly, for this requires nourishment from large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures come in many different ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all the ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is breaking that would go to war, and another when sharpening, such as the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with breaking due to injury, and breaking with a small crack in its entirety.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each way has its own tool, and its proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and by this one knows the breakage of the bone through the fact that the limb is twisted, and opens well outward, and is at the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or curvature in its location, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But if you cannot move it by hand, then apply the remedies that follow next, and then gently manipulate it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that when the bone is broken and the two parts are disjoined, now you should put them at an equal point so that abscesses can form on either side.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if pus forms during this period, if he leaves it for any day, until the abscess subsides;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then place it at the same level as you can slightly and gently squeeze, and know that restoring it is easier than when he has pieces; then you restrain him, just as prescribed below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are pieces in the bone, if it is split into two parts, whether they be hands or feet, or at your hand if it's a small limb, or into two strings, or one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the member are healed, you tighten all around using whatever means you can, and guard that in your work no injury or pain befalls the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And correctly adjust the two shoulder joints according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if it doesn't seem to be perfectly located: if it is dressed beautifully, and not strained too much, without squeezing as those who bring out abscesses by their work do, just like we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, carefully restrain the patient so they do not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, neither upon turning, nor in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And see to it that the limb is secured enough so that there is no feeling of pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at the exact spot, and it should be placed in such arrangement that he does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep him straight, so no twisting occurs when he is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the limb broken is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are various in size and extent, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs such as arms and legs and alike: it is necessary to envelop them with soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And those that are larger, such as the buttocks and calves: it is necessary to envelop them with a broad and firm bandage; for wide bands wrap around the entire large limb, restraining it evenly from all sides, so no bulge remains;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then wrap in light bandages, three times or four times depending on the limb, and press your hand slightly along the entire bandage, then go over the breakage and tighten it less, so that the breakage moves a little away from the wound.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And gradually soften the tie a little by little, until you grasp a large portion of the healthy part, then take another tie, and return to its original position on the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the broken part and gently tighten it, neither too hard nor too soft, as we have said in our first instruction above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the linen straps or bandages evenly, until it is completely even, then tie everything above with two belts, and then put your well-made pins on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing on it that relieves the abscess and reduces the swelling, leaving it like this for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then hold onto these poles, and they should be half as wide as a narrow reed bent straightly, or from the shaft used to make darts, or from the branches of a palm tree, and they should follow this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the pole which one places at the break be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it be as long as necessary for small or large limbs;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold them in place just like you did at the first instance, then tie an additional thread on top of it, similarly to how you tied at the break in the first instance;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	The cautery should allow the hair to grow long and even; if they prick at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, like those used in folk works to twist their linen cords, and this is a great mistake, because the twist cannot be uniform if it's too thin, and it doesn't suit having less than one and a half inches of space between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the limbs are bruised by the joints of the sockets after reduction in their healthy positions, then apply padding with linen or shredded wool on them, so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is due to piercing (or stab) injury, and the ribs are broken, I will instruct on its treatment thereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	Know that it's not suitable to fully stretch all the broken limbs right from the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it's not suitable to place them in splints straightaway; rather wait for at least five days or seven, or longer according to your judgment as each case arises.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of the old plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: you take flour that remains on the walls of the mill, mix it with enough egg until the mixture isn't too thin or too thick. Use this concoction, and this is the common way of using plaster to restore fractures in various ways, as well as for women and small children, because there's no risk of being too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method for setting breaks and dislocations and twists: take three parts of garlic and dill and wormwood and asafetida and Arabic gum and mastic, in total. Use five parts of myrrh and aloes, also in total. Add seven parts of alechil. Grind all these into a powder, then mix them with the yolk of an egg; if the mixture is warm, use this plaster as it has a good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, proving beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plastering method that is good for twists: take mastic and vismarrow, in total ten parts; myrrh and aloes, in total eight parts; acacia six parts; Armenian galbanum ten parts, grind them well together, then mix with water or the yolk of an egg, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another plastering method for joints and broken bones, to alleviate the pain that comes with them, and to cut away bone fragments: take new wool, cook it in grease and oil until it softens, then apply it onto the affected area. This plaster does not heal completely but is better for soothing abscesses, and properly relieves pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plastering that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and terrestrial oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plastering for restoring bone fractures and facilitating the removal of pus. Take root of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of beeswax; from each take one part; grind it together, mix with wine, and if your limbs are warm, mix it with moist coriander water or just water, and then use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another more effective method of plastering when pus is being restored in the limb. Take roots of valerian, linseed, balm, linden and thyme, as well as violet and chamomile flowers; from each take one part; grind it together, mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine according to the warmth of the limb and its rest period.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates instructs that one should apply to the broken limb for strength restoration using a paste made of wax and oil, and nothing else, more. He says it should be neither too soft nor too hard between two states.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen suggests one should apply to the broken limb for restoration dry things slightly warm, such as mire, aloe, incense, and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make plaster useful for injury and pain: take mussels and pigeon meat or bird feathers, and basil leaves, and equal parts of wine vinegar, grind them together, and then make a plaster with it and use it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then after a little while, take care to ensure that the patient does not feel any pain and that there is no movement of their bone in its place; or if the injury is treated by hand during the day.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the arm, or itching, without rest or swelling, you should act quickly, and release it, and apply plaster now; and take light cloth and a moistened sponge from the sea, immerse them in water, and cool down the arm until the itching stops, and the pain is alleviated.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool, moistened in water or oil from the rose bush, and secure it with a bandage, until you are sure of removing any pus.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation settle on the member, and relieve the pain, then resume gentle treatment, and a little plaster, but do not strain it as much as before; and be gentle until it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that pus and redness, pain and swelling are present throughout the bone, and you need to plaster and bind it, then repeat as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if there is nothing of what we have said on the limb, or if it's released only after three days, four days, five days, or seven; and leave it for twenty days each time, according to this until healing progresses, and approaches bone setting in place;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then increase the bandaging more than at first, and let it grow its flesh, just as I said previously. And if you see that the body dries excessively beyond what is necessary, know that there will be no improvement;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	The first sentence translates as:
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this work then correct the deformities in the limb, and remedy it quickly as what men do, that restore the member forcibly: this is bad, and such actions lead to useless procedures, and I see nothing else but to leave them and treat them correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of fracturing
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of breaking exist, and various forms, and the causes are destined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For it involves injuries caused by striking with a sword, and the neck bone all the way to the syfac which is under the bone, just like in an axe or staff; and because of this, this kind of injury is called 'axe break' in this manner.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing it, this kind of injury is called 'absolute break'; and it refers to the wounds resulting from these two types of breaks, whether large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential striking, or crack, or from the stone itself, or impact on the stone, or other similar incidents.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a partial break, which approaches until it reaches the tissue under the bone, or above the bone, and this injury can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that has healed within the bone as thin as a hair, and has a small crack, and because of this it is called this kind of fracture "hairline";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound made or by piercing of stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and it lets the piece of bone in from below, and has cuts next to each other like candle makers when they make holes on the candles; so that the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	This happens more with those who have wet bones below, such as children's bones;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	It occurs in all these ways of fracture where small pieces are dismembered, like fowl's bones; and I will speak about this in its proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all methods of fractures through their dislocation upon them, and the examination by prodding, and through the decayed flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	Hair loss is known by those who when an osseous fragment has been revealed and rubbed together, if it exposes black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be cautious about malaise incidents, and if you do not see any ill-omened accidents such as vomiting, loss of understanding, expansion, paleness, fever, or if the eyes start to come out and turn red, or show other symptoms in various conditions, there is no certainty that it can heal.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accidents, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the bone comes to you first, and it's in winter, if you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day after your arrival that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, you should remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh around the bone becomes rotten, and accidents as we've said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture reaches to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary for you to split the fractured part like this: and take hold of the bone from the patient's arm, uncover over the bone in all manners that you can, and expose more of the wound according to its shape as much as you can,
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood flow starts to reveal the bone, or an abscess appears, assist with what is necessary, and make sure you fill the wound with wet cloths in oil rose.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And have the wound rest until the pus discharge is calmed and the blood can freely flow; then begin working inside the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut at a narrow angle in front, and it's called:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut, which is larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, all sharp, and made of iron; and work with light hands, making sure not to pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and beyond piercing, you should pierce it through, ensuring that you make cuts with steady hands, not all the way through so as not to penetrate beyond the bone by mistake, and there should be a margin or circle of about an inch above the tip, preventing the tip from passing through the bone; and you should have several of them, so each touches its length of the bone, ensuring that there are tines for both sides; this is the form of the three methods of piercing.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce inside the broken bone is that you place one wick on the bone and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone has been pierced. Then put the wick elsewhere a little after, and do this throughout, then cut in between the roots of the teeth where the bone exists, and do this more subtly than you can, gently, just as we have said, till you pull the bone to your hand or to none of the instruments that you have such as pliers, forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain nor the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, it is necessary that you prepare what was left of the bone with another tool similar to a tooth, but this tool should be more sturdy and more subtle than the other tooth;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there is nothing of the small bones or no scales left, you should gently scrape them with an instrument. Then dress and treat the wound as we have said earlier.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of treatment is this as Galien said, which is more safe; and the needle is very strong, and it's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you must expose a part of the bone where the fracture opens and moves. So when you have exposed that part, place underneath the edge of this lens-shaped incision, as depicted here:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side alone, and make the incision halfway through two ribs so that when you cut it is towards the bone. Then strike with a small hammer from above, gently removing all of the bone and being careful not to damage the membrane which is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If she presses against the bone, gently remove it because you will feel no harm and little fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then after that roughness, it's necessary to remove the scales with a sharp shaver of which you should have various quantities. To administer each one as most appropriate according to the manual and the appearance of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you appear before great shavers, and then even finer ones, and don't stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and finer breaks, you must administer care according to its direction; and this matter is not resolved for whoever has devoted their study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the shoulder's wound is revealed, it is necessary that you take one and a half linen cloths according to the size of the injury, soak them in rose oil, and place them on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another double linen cloth or two, and soak them in wine and rose oil, place it on the first linen cloth; do this more lightly than you can, so as not to burden the shoulder blade, then apply with a second bandage, but don't strain it too hard that it only touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess softens, then remove the bandage and apply remedies such as lily roots, flour of myrrh, incense powder, and aristolochia, among other things; prepare a powder from these and apply it to the wound, then continue applying gentle healing medicines without causing irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And ensure that the wound is clean right away, do not leave pus behind, and do not allow any fluid to assemble there either, because when fluid assembles on the brain's membrane, it circulates and spreads, causing great harm to the patient; for when one places something biting on the tongue, it bites from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore take care, if nothing happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if only that happened because of the medicine we put on, assuming it has such a virtue, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them in a spoonful, and put this on the tongue;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then follow the method of treatment until they become healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts under the nose or even just one, because these are two bones; and this lower part is made of cartilage, it does not break, nor will it take to bend or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must bend your little finger or over the nose, and make an equal break inside to your second finger, and through the tip outward, until the nose revives according to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your operation.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the area above the nose, and cannot reach the nostril from below, it should be positioned evenly to the top of a small stick that's a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, redo the procedure and try to restore on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or eighth day when the abscess has subsided, apply to the top of the nose a bundle made from linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you should apply a bundle on the other side as well, if the fracture is there too; and make them large enough to fill out the hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And it's said that one should moisten the tents with butter and change them each day. I do not think this is correct but rather they should be moistened during the preparation of a mixture of egg white and powder of grinding stone; then leave the tent until the bone is hard and the cartilage tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one uses goose feathers instead of tents, and if it's mixed with one egg white, and if there is a wind, and the air goes among them; then do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses appear near the nose as you do them, then put wadding or moistened cotton in oil of rose, or a pinch of salt.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses do not appear, then apply a plaster outside, made of ash powder and incense powder, mixed with yolk butter. Place it on light bandages, don't tie them tightly around the nose;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the nose breaks into small pieces and it is broken into many parts, then use tools suitable for this task, then cut along the wound, and clean all the fragments of cartilage and suture them. If there are applicable plasters or ointments for this situation, use them;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the nose, then treat with tinctures and apply linseed oil until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured internally and there is no external wound,
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary; if the fracture is in the right part, you bend your index finger into the patient's mouth towards the side of the injury. And if the fracture is in the left jawbone, then bend your index finger of the right hand towards it, and gently apply pressure on the fracture internally, and perform this action with the other hand externally, making sure to do so evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is separated into two parts, then it's necessary to administer an extension for each part until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth occur, or rupture, then restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk. Place it on the broken mandible and place one double piece of cloth; and put another large tent on the cloth well made, or an equal piece of leather long and wide according to the length of the mandible, and bind it up as tight as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, let it shift to its position on the third day and then adjust what has changed; cover with plaster, using powder from a mill combined with plenty of egg or ground oyster flour after removing the bandage; place a layer of wool on top, and when the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition doesn't change, let it be until they recover. Many times recovery occurs within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if pus-filled sores appear, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture combined with a wound, it's rewarded by none of the bone being extracted; if the extraction requires instruments suitable for this task.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is nothing left, if the wound is wide, place one layer of plasters suitable for it to accelerate healing until it heals.
de la forcele	By the power.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.
