And if no such incidents occur, or if the dislocation is not relieved until two days later or more, let the pain remain on their back and keep their hands on their stomach; then place under the shoulder one clean cloth of equal wool for each hour of the day or night, watching that the figure of the broken limb does not move or that the ligaments do not soften; if it heals through the power of medicine, and gives them the meat we placed before in such a way that the meat becomes as fine as possible; and when they start to recover, let it be large. And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to take recovery for forty days total; then you should remove and administer baths and medications for treating the area effectively. If the dislocation is ugly or twisted, let it remain in relief for two days or a month.
de la brisure du bras	"Of the breaking of the arm"
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the pair 'foscile'. One bone is small, and it's this one that covers the elbow; and the other bone is large, and it's this one that lies underneath, towards the little finger. By chance, only the larger foscile breaks or both could break, or they might come together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bones break, the restoration is light and the healing; and when the large ones break, then the healing goes badly, and worse than when they broke together. If it's only the small bone that breaks, then slight stretching should be done, and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the larger bone that breaks, then one needs to strain harder; and stretch it on two cushions, and raise the hand of the patient higher than the others, and place the small finger lower than the other fingers, and have the limb cross over itself, with another cushion in front higher than necessary so no discomfort is felt; then extend his assistant's arm up to where their elbow lies beneath their hand or at one's wrist, and a helper at one's other side above. And then place the arm of the patient level according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if during the breaking into pieces, you place each in its place, and if there is none that sticks to the bone when you grasp it, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do on and with the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if during the healing process, I mentioned it in a separate chapter; if take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if during the beginning of the restoration process wounds occur, apply this: take a plaster made from rosin and white beeswax, ensuring it is neither too hard nor too soft; then place one sheet of plaster carefully above each other until all the wounds have calmed. After that remove the plaster, and then apply the paste made from mill-ground powder with enough egg. Place the splints, making sure they are further up in the healing process than elsewhere, slightly wider than on other parts, and note that there should be seven or eight splint positions: either if it's within one bone, or two bones; keep them higher around the healing process rather than other places, and every day move less far away from their original position as I have mentioned at the beginning of this chapter. Ensure that all materials covering the healing process are soft and moistened, neither too hard nor abrasive; use threads made from linen, not too thick or thin, as we've discussed. Lastly, care for the limb and its wound over several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad incidents come to the member, for example itchiness coming to the member, it is necessary that you immerse the member in hot water until the itch subsides; and leave the member not moved to rest. And then start tightening again, and if the band has been broken and the bone uncovered, doing something similar, then place it correctly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if precautions are taken so that no stiffness comes to the member, because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it by rubbing, and let it rest for a few days, until the stiffness passes, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have said comes to the patient or it's healing doesn't progress up to twenty days, then you can undo the bandage. Afterwards, place your hands on their neck and ensure that both sides are equal, while guarding against movement and strain, and let them sleep on their back; and know that this healing is restored in thirty days or forty days, and sometimes in twenty days, depending on the nature of the remedies and their individual constitution.
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You should know that on the back of the hand and around our thumbs there are few injuries, and it only causes many plagues.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is broken or swelled, it is necessary for the patient to lie with their palm facing up and straight ahead as well; then they should place their hand on an extended surface, extend their fingers over the broken bones, and align them evenly until they are properly connected; and they should apply bandages and splints, if no abscesses develop, then they should place a splint according to the size of their hand; and it should be wrapped in one linen sheet.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the injury is located at or near the belly of the sole, then make a bundle with cloths, and instruct the patient to place this on their broken foot; and then apply a long cloth wrap, and have them wear a splint that fits as well as possible for the size of their hand, just like they would for their entire hand.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the front, it should be that you place one pin above and another under in the foot, so that the hands are open and straight, then tie them altogether under the hand, and seal off the connection between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of our fingers, if it is in the middle, as it should be; and bind with the foot, and if you see that place a small pin upright to lift the break, and do not move; and if the break is at another finger, such as in the index or one of the others, then place it evenly, and tie with the healthy finger which comes after; or you tie all together holding them, so they don't move, or you put a pin there as for when we fix it. And take care in the restoration and positioning of each abscess, and apply what comes to that person, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken foot
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the knee is broken many times, and one can see it often when it turns forward and backward; and its repair consists in joining .1 above the breakage, and another .1 below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the limbs lie on their face, then extend each minister his link to its equal part; and this is when the breakage is inside the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the breakage is near the knee joint, then have one of the links towards the foot, and the other links below the breakage. And likewise if it's near the hip, then put the joints in front of the hip, and thus make the extension upwards; then place the eyes on the bone equally with its two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then apply plaster, and the link, so that no abscesses come about.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is pus at the site, let it heal then return to your work and treatment; the operation has been performed in such manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you envelop around the wound; i.e., bind it with a bandage doubled in two or three parts, and retain excess material. Then lift the leg so that the heel reaches to the base of the shinbone, and insert one thread long between the skin and the leg, down through the knee, and guide the end of the thread upwards; then begin enveloping around the leg and the thigh with the bandage, place a stake at the wound site, and put a stake at the bone of the leg; then place four pieces of cloth under the leg and the thigh to maintain even pressure. Begin binding around the wound in three or four turns; and as you go above the wound, bind less tightly; then attach two thread ends that you have inserted between the leg and the thigh, and bind them with three stakes that are up there, then return below to where the thread end is, until you reach under the foot; and tighten, so it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, then if there is pus or swelling or any other symptoms.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, set it free, and address whatever comes up, just as we have said many times. And if there are pieces of bone that catch hold, it's right to remove them, provided they can be removed; and if you cannot, then it's right to cut the wound open, and drain the pus; and treat it in such a way as we have said, until it heals completely.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the wrist broken when one places them like this, as in the shoulder and arm; still, no complaint from the patient follows such a restoration.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the wrist is restored in one or two days, or perhaps less or perhaps more, depending on the variety of physiques.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the gallbladder
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the gallbladder alley there is little breaking, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it's usually just a crack, or a small tear of about an inch, and occurs with or without injury, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: if you place it evenly with what's round at its ends until they are assembled and moveable, then apply plaster. And put an oval piece on top if you need to, and tighten it according to how it should be done, then redo all the arrangements we've talked about in other injuries, like pus and similar; for each condition put what suits it, as long as it's sound.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You know that in the leg there are two bones. One of them is called 'right non' which means 'tibia', and the other one is called 'foscile' meaning 'fibula'. And any kind of injury or breakage can happen to it just like with the arm, and for this, the restoration process is similar to that of an arm, equally, and all the procedures are exactly the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg from every side.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bones are broken, one feels intense pain and sees it clearly; then turn immediately. Therefore apply extension, place them equally, and tie the ligaments equally; but still, when the break is irregular and consists of several pieces, make sure that the extension is less extensive and lighter; and align them according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two lengths of checked wood that bend the leg on one side and the other, and let them be as long as half the length of the leg from the knee to below; then wrap these in two layers of twine over and under, and tie them in the middle so that the leg cannot lean to the right or left; thus it is well; and no one should apply a single strip this length made of wood for the leg, and place it on guard against any movement. It must be properly done at the break where there is injury; and move the leg each day, to see if there is any pus or other incident; continue the cure until it is sane.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of bone fracture due to impact
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no breakage, but with bone impact breakage occurs and in the lower leg bones, it only results from shaking under various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is an impact breakage at the bones in the leg, and you see these bones press one against another, place them like bones on the ground, just as if they wanted to go, and then put your foot on his ankle, where the bones are raised, push them as much as it takes for them to return to their sockets; then apply plaster and bandages around this side of the leg, and place a small table under both ankles, each filled with about two inches. Then press against the leg up to its bending point, then when you have wrapped cloths around them, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you remove the bandage, because you will find that the bones are even, whether broken or re-aligned.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the ribs are broken, repair them as we said about the ribs of the hand. Then put a splint on the broken rib according to its length, and make it slightly wider than that, then place under the foot this board I spoke of, and apply even pressure; and if there are two or three, or more, break them, put one splint on each rib according to their size, wrapped in one linen sheet, and hold the table against the foot. And being on the head of the table facing towards the belly of the foot, make sure it is well positioned.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I've said about other injuries, just as we have discussed; and assist each case according to how it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of its nature in a woman is broken, have her sit with it swollen and enlarged. Then incline her to the lower part of her backside and hold her at the rear. Next fill up the gap of nature with cotton, placing equal quantities as would be about one hand. After that take out the woman and lift her bottom gradually and little by little; then let the cotton fall until it reaches the entrance of nature, bringing the bone with it. And when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton; upon her finishing, return her to normal again; thus repeat this process for seven days or more: if restoration has occurred, take a kid's bladder and tie onto its tip a stick; fill up the whole bladder in nature. Then inflate into the stick forcefully until the bladder swells internally; this will help restore the breakage. Next, fill with cotton and let it stay like that for some more days till it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the elbow in a man is broken, or for a woman, restore it as we have said about the thigh bone; and these broken bones are not to be overlooked by those who apply their skill and use them, and heed my book. For breaking indicates in various positions the correct path of restoration: thus understand it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of the penis if it is broken, take a goose’s throat and fill the penis with it; then wrap bandages around it, and let it be for three days or as long as needed, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	From fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the person with a fracture that also has a wound, even if it's large, like in the case of bones in the elbow or shoulder or similar, to be now cleaned, so that the cleanings which we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, you can fumigate it with vitriol (sulfuric acid), and if you don't have anything else, then start restoring the fracture in that same hour or day; or when abscesses do not appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscesses start appearing, let the restoration continue for another day or two, until the abscess subsides, and don't touch it on the third or fourth day, because you might provoke a harmful incident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if bone is broken and visible at the site of the open wound, it is necessary to place your hands on it gently, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not present for you to align evenly with your hands, take this iron instrument that is made of steel, which is seven inches or six inches long, and the width should match the size of the wound; and for this purpose, the surgeon must choose three or four (depending on what he needs for each treatment of bone fracture), and it should be round and a bit large so that it doesn't bend under compression against your limb during surgery, and it should have points at the front, and be thick in the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And call it "palainche", because it is necessary that the curved bones be placed on the top of the visible bone; and strike once with it, until it returns, and make them equal one against another. And if the fracture is thin, and the instruments cannot properly grasp the bone, it is necessary that you hold the tip of the bone, as long as the instrument has the ability to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone to its place, as we have said, if you have an appropriate tool for this purpose, such as a scalpel or a fine awl, then with your strength; then reposition that which is staying in the hard part of the bone and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone has been put back in place, and if there is intense pain from the patient afterwards, know that it hasn't returned to its natural position. Do not force it into position, instead moisten it with one part of alcohol mixed with black laudanum, and properly if it's in its original state; and do not apply any ointment or other substances where there is pus, so as to prevent the development of putrefaction and decay; then administer these measures when you have set the bone, and leave the wound exposed, and cover it entirely according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained by pressure; many times this has been done, leading to death or corrosion in some cases; and let the straining be softer and more gentle than other injuries; and thus, many have seen the patient recover.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that any adverse events will occur there, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, it should not be treated with these measures; but cover it entirely instead, in place of these measures, with hard cloths and bind them. And when after one or two days you see an improvement or some healing on the wound, then remove whatever you had placed over it with all the wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as the four-formula ointment and similar treatments.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary for you to dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is united and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should be so that the joints of the limb are put together in such a way that the bone slips down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if this continues day after day, and it cannot be joined but stays like that, know that there are small bone pieces causing pain due to which you should cover the wound with a tent, and remove all these pieces of dead tissue that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes about in the body, or any other form of decay, it must be treated according to what he instructs in his previous chapter. And when bone is broken and exposed within the limb, such as in the case of bones in the foot or shoulder, or similar large limb bones, they should not be treated immediately because death may occur from them many times; however, leave them until they heal, perhaps after 20 to 30 days, then treat the wound if possible; and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The burns come many times after the healing of the burn wound, even when it's close to the joint. A strange thing is to see the shape of the limb; and by chance it cannot perform its natural acts on the limb.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore when this thing is fresh: if you administer stiffening medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, along with sarsaparilla, licorice, and other similar things, do so according to your preference or combine them all, mixing them with stictic wine or with plenty of egg or with garlic; then apply them on the wound in poultices, apply them well, and don't remove it by hand for days; then remove it, and start another poultice as long as the pustules are removed; or you can apply over a piece of plaster that has been made properly; because the properties of plaster allow to remove all swellings from the limbs; and if the pustule has hardened like stone and needs removal, cut through it from above, revealing excess fluid; or have it sanded by someone until it is removed, and continue treatment until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb which becomes weak after the siege (or after a period of confinement or hard work)
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and afterwards the limbs remain weak and delicate, this can happen for various reasons: due to which it was bound too tightly and wasn't bound as it should have been; or due to there being too many bindings, and not being able to bring the respiration to the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to too large movements, not in its time; or due to having little blood in his body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat well, and make the body soft until the healing spreads in him; then give them baths, and provide them joy and comfort. Then apply grease on the limb so that the grease attracts to the main respiration, and washes it with water often, until the respiration matches the limb. And restore its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is twisted after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken openly, and the shape of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: nor should one believe those who say that we must break the entire limb anew. And many foolish people have done this in our land; these procedures are criticized, and they bring great harms, even causing death at times. However, if the dislocations and pains are still fresh, you should heat them with hot water or cook soothing herbs such as leaves of comfrey, roots, and mallow, among others; and apply a moistening plaster, like well-made yarrow. You take the comfrey sap and mix it with lard or oil from saffron, and make a plaster from that; or you take greased figs, grind them with bran, and other medicines that are made soothing by heating.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And never stop to moisten the dislocation and keep rubbing it for a long time with wet hands. And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation has become old and hardened like bone, requiring treatment with an iron instrument, so it should be cut up to the bone at a subtle incision lightly; and place supervision and diligence in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the body.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects no particular area but now requires immediate restoration without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the limbs swell up, and by chance it might be set back to its original position in pain; because you should not move it at the moment when it is swollen: many times it brings on pus and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	If this happens, if you have a surgeon for the patient, then let him stay until all abscesses are subdued; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each limb according to where treatment comes naturally.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on shoulder dislocations up until here.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated and downwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are somewhat ossified at their joints and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the feet, causing saliva from the mouth to spill out, and preventing them from closing their mouths, as well as wrapping their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it can return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it's complete and has been fully displaced, then you should reset it quickly without hesitation;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in this manner, have the assistants cut at the head's place where there are hairs, and with one hand push her cheekbones into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth; if it's a dislocation of two parts; and let the other hand be out to match. And instruct the patient to soften and move their jaws in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And keep pushing until she wakes up in her place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it causes pain, in the same way, if they are two jaws together, then use hot water and oil, as long as you gently reset them; don't overly force the return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes properly after being made milder, then place moist cloths in a poultice made from olive oil and beeswax, then bind them gently with moist threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on their back, and have their head resting between two cushions, so that they do not move to either side or force themselves to turn, but consume light food until the pains are reduced, and ensure that their jaws are closed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then taste this so that it can be eaten lightly, and does not cause the opening of the mouth during eating or drinking until the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set properly within an hour and are not returned to their original position, this results in fevers and recurrent illnesses, as well as occasional abdominal discomfort or vomiting.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is loss; and many times, death befalls the one who experiences it within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the forcefulness
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strength cannot relieve the pain from within or below, it relieves only when outside, and one certainly feels this.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the process is that when the patient lies on their back and extends their arms; and then presses them into your palm, they will return. Then place them on a plaster and wrap the bandage around, and keep it tight;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the shoulder that is towards the knife cannot relieve itself; if it does not and if it relieves once, then reset it to its place as we have said; then place it on a plaster and wrap the bandage around, and keep it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, bring back the shoulder of the spine when it is freed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	On the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in two ways: one way is when it dislocates towards the side of the armpit downwards; and the second way is at the part below the buttocks; and by chance it dislocates upwards, which happens less often;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside through the nerves; and many times dislocates towards the armpit for those who have little flesh, because when they jump, the shoulder goes in quickly; for those who have enough flesh, it jumps to the elbow bone and then returns to it.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens in some men due to impact or bruising, and the shoulder swells up with an abscess and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you must verify it as long as you are sure about it; and only after that start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And recognize dislocations when they are directed towards the shoulder blade, and make a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them an evident diversity.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and from the shoulder blade to the armpit, as if it were a hole; and the patient cannot bring his hand back to his nose, nor move in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated upwards and not hidden, you find it clearly at the armpit;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this method of dislocation must be to reset it when it's new or if it affects the child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts his hand from the ailment up top, then places his fingers on the surface, and lifts the joint up forcefully to its original position; and the minister lifts his hand, extends it upwards, placing it onto [the affected area]; if it moves too quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it doesn't come like we have said within days afterwards, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the minister should administer a soothing treatment, as with decoctions of marjoram, fenugreek, and chamomile in hot water, and apply it.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then cover the patient's back with a cloth, and place on the surface a padding of equal thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the heel of the foot on the padding, and raise the head of the shoulder gently, and guide the hand towards the ailment.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another servant cuts the neck of the patient so it doesn't move forward; this shoulder comes back right now, and if you see that you reset it according to this method:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And you should have someone present at your home who is bigger than the patient; and be upright towards the side, and push the shoulder under the collarbone of the patient, and lift up the collarbone, so that the head hangs vertically.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another servant pulls the hand of the patient backward towards the belly. And if the head is too light, and nothing heavy is placed on him, then the dislocation comes back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And you also reset it in another way: and one sticks a long stick into the ground, so that the head of the shoulder is placed as with a bullet, and not too large nor too slippery;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then place some over the hair, but have a shield underneath it, and let the hair stay as long as that of the stick. Then extend her hand down on the other side diagonally, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if she doesn't return with all these things that we have said, do this treatment: take one rod of two strong and four thick, which allows the head to fit in by force from below at an angle, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then bind the head to the stick under a shield so that the stick doesn't hurt the hair, then place the stick on the shoulder at an angle with the hair; and extend your arm up along the stick as long as possible, then tie the support on the stick, and the arm below the head, then put the arm on one of two thick rods, about four inches wide, and have your hand extended downwards, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return to its place right now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, in whatever manner, if you need to place an equal thread on the shoulder joint, then apply plaster powder mixed with mill dust, along with incense and yolk butter, all over the shoulder and around it, then remove from the shoulder area, and retie above the plaster dressing, and secure the bandage again on top of the plaster, and hold hands to their necks, and keep the hands in this manner.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat a little, until the body parts are strengthened, because he will heal faster; and then increase his intake after about 5 days or 10 days, and move him; and if it is firm and not softened, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is loose due to moisture that has caused it, or for another reason, you should administer three applications of cauterization to it, as was described in the section on cauterizations before this chapter.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder has been stretched or weakened; and know that the joint would never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations near the buttocks, breasts, or behind, are caused by hand thrust and stretching, and occur elsewhere too; treat until it becomes clear.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there's pain in the limb, and delays in movement, then immerse the patient in warm baths repeatedly, until this pain subsides, and returns to their original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	From the dislocation of the shoulder bone.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure. Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in this way for abscesses to be extracted completely, because if they were extracted partially and left behind, it would be difficult to remove them; and by chance, it may not be able to be removed entirely, even when it's at the back. It is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance it can lead to death.

And for its restoration if it can be returned to this condition, you should extend his hand with both of your hands; and his arms shall be spread outwards, downwards and upwards, and place the fingers towards the elbow along the inside, outside and underneath, then press the joint onto his shoulder blades or at the root of his palm until it regains its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand against itself, and places the cut on the root of the palm that was dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it doesn't return to its place, apply strong extension; and have both of you extend the arm, and do this with both hands so that it does not move during extension. Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie. et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it sweats, rub the joint gently, then set the bone back in place, and afterwards into a bath; and do this twice or three times until it feels better; and if you can see that it helps, apply moist cow fat heated with butter to it, and leave it on; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut. des dislocations de la hainche	On the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier. The hip joint is dislocated in four ways: internally and externally, forwards and backwards; more internally than externally, less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of internal dislocations is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and the diseased knee opens more than the healthy one, and the diseased knee cannot bend to reach fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is where the limbs are swollen due to an abscess, because the head of the thigh bone comes into play.

Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs for him who is coming to what lies ahead, it means that his leg is well according to completion; however, neither doubles nor stretches his knee without pain, and if one tries to make him move forward, he cannot before and retains his urine, and swells his ankle, and when he walks, he does so on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes. Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocations are in front, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg promptly, and according to what I have said; and place the pain of being on the bad side, then press with the other hand, and pull forward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocations are at the back, it is not necessary to extend the leg behind or lift onto the ground, but rather the limb should be in the same position as when the hip was dislocated at the back, just like we said about lying on the two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And lie on their face, and extend the joint like we have said before, and one must press at the joint on the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	And it will be ready when the patient extends their legs and they are of equal length. Then adjust their hips and apply a plaster, and bind them with a bandage so that they do not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And they rest for three or four days, then release them and apply the plaster. And if you see that they are of equal length, bind them as before, and leave them for another three days. Then release them again and let them move well, until the limbs have become strong.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knees can be dislocated in two ways: this means, internally and externally, and behind; and they do not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at their knee, and if they cannot reach their knee, you know they are dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of everything is that you make the patient stand straight, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back against their thigh, and set their foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take their kneecap in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee together; and another attendant extends their foot until the knee returns to its place. And the signs are that they nicely move their leg at the knee gently.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	put the bandage on, and allow the leg to rest at the knee, then join them tightly for three or four days, then release. And do not move the injured limbs until they are healed, as long as the body parts have been strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb is not yet at all, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip joint, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never properly set and never fully released, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs for this are that the ankle swells up, and tends forward to the part where it was dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The movement should be swift; one must gently extend their hands when they are merely stretched out.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it has come back to its place entirely, it is necessary that you make the patient sit up straight, and hold him with two attendants behind by his leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then again with your left hand, four times, then lift up and firmly hold the foot high;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	And do this twice, as we have said, while holding and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is well; if not, begin the process again, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	And if it cannot return like this, then release the patient's back towards the ground, and place a stick, and push it firmly into the earth between its buttocks, and tie cloths around it, so that it does not bruise the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then scrape his thighs, and other attendants spread his feet to his hands or under one tie, so they are bound around the neck of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then extend each attendant evenly, and let the stick stay between the thighs of the patient to hold the thigh in place when one extends it.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then position both shoulders evenly at the patient's hands, and other attendants scrape the healthy leg up to the knee, and the dislocated shoulder will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is at its point, place the plaster and apply hot iron over it, hold it in place firmly, and tie the stick to the leg, guard against the nerves that are behind the ankle, so they are not too tight;
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage comes loose, hold it in place again; then release it on the third day or fourth, and gently guide the patient for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he moves beyond this period, it is not secure that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pus comes out, you should soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	From these two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both shoulders are dislocated, if they suit well to extend them by work, and this is a slight matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocations are in neither back nor seat bones, you should have the patient sit on or on the end of their back, making sure it is perfectly flat or on a table completely upright, and place your foot on what opens from these joints, then press with your foot firmly until they regain consciousness;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when they are level and there is nothing open, place a bench of two stools under the foot's sole, then press firmly, and let it stay for three days, then release him; and have him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Regarding wounds and dislocations combined
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one seeks to restore it, many times the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the treatment, if you are wise in the art and have used it for a long time, and if you are compassionate and merciful but not hasty;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and begin with soothing things for the abscess to drain, and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope of recovery;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, reset the limb back to its place immediately, so that the abscesses can drain and heal.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is back in place, apply soothing ointments to the abscesses and treat the wound as it should be treated, using dried healing substances.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if there is breaking with dislocation and small fractures, set the bones, and do as we have instructed for simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And beware not to fall into the path of fear, as I have said, for this is what your Creator commands you to do, and through knowledge protect yourself and your body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Here comes the first sentence to translate.
